ثم الدليل عندنا من طريق القرآن على لزوم القول بخلق الأفعال قوله: ﴿وأسرُّوا قولكم أو اجهروا به إنه عليم بذات الصدور ألا يعلم من خلق وهو اللطيف الخبير﴾ [الملك، ١٣-١٤]، فلو لم يكن جل ثناؤه خالقاً لما يُجهر ويُخفى لم يكن ليحتج به على علمه. ومعلوم جواز الجهل من غير الذي يفعله، فإذا لم يكن للاحتجاج بفعل سواه معنى. وأيضاً إن الله تعالى قال: ﴿هو الذي يسيّركم في البر والبحر﴾ [يونس، ٢٢]، وقال في موضع آخر: ﴿وقدرنا فيها السير سيروا فيها ليالي﴾ [سبأ، ١٨]، أخبر أن تقدير السير والتسيير فعله، وبه كان السير ومن كان يسير. وقال: ﴿ومن آياته أن خلق لكم من أنفسكم أزواجاً لتسكنوا إليها وجعل بينكم مودة ورحمة﴾ [الروم، ٢١]، فيها خبر أن جعل المودة والرحمة من آياته، وأن منامكم من آياته وابتغاءكم من فضله من آياته. ومن البعيد إنشاء غيره له من الآيات؛ إذ ذلك الفاعل أحق أن تكون الآية له، وهن كلهن أفعال الخلق. وقال: ﴿وجعلنا في قلوب الذين اتبعوه رأفة ورحمة﴾ [الحديد، ٢٧]، وقال: ﴿أولئك كتب في قلوبهم الإيمان﴾ [المجادلة، ٢٢]، وقال: ﴿وجعل لكم من جلود الأنعام بيوتاً﴾ [النحل، ٨٠]، وقال: ﴿وجعلنا قلوبهم قاسية﴾ [المائدة، ١٣]. وفي الجملة قال الله: ﴿فعّال لما يريد﴾، وفي أفعال العباد ما يريد، وقد وعد أن يفعل ما يريد. وقد ذم الله من أحب أن يُحمد على ما لم يفعل، وقد ألزم المؤمنين أن يحمدوه على الإيمان، فثبت أن ذلك بفعله. ولا قوة إلا بالله.

والأصل فيه أن دلالة خلق فعل كل أحد عنده أعظم من دلالة خلق السموات والأرض فيما أريد تعرف حقيقة ذلك بالعقل؛ إنه لا أحد امتحن قوى جواهر العالم حتى يعلم خروج كل شيء عن ذلك واحتمال خلق مثله، بل إنما يعرف ذلك بخروجه عن إمكان مثله. ومعلوم وجود أمور في غيره من الجواهر مما امتنع جوهره عن احتمال ذلك، نحو الطيران وإخراق الأشياء والسباحة بالجواهر وغير ذلك بقوى فيها. ويعلم كل أن ليس لأحد من الخلق تدبير في فعله؛ فيعلم بالضرورة بما خرج عن مقصوده وقصر عن الحد الذي يحده، وكان مقدّراً بما لا يحتمل وسعه التقدير به، فيعلم به ضرورةً أن الذي به قام هو الذي قدّره وأخرجه على ما أراد ولا قوة إلا بالله.

مع ما لم يكن عند المعتزلة من الله إلى خلقه جملة سوى أنه أوجده بعد أن لم يكن، وأن الله لم يزل موجوداً؛ وذلك المعنى في فعل كل أحد موجود. على أنه لولا الأمر والنهي لم يكن العقل يحتمل إخراج شيء عن قدرة الله وصرف شيء إلى فعل غيره. والأمر والنهي في محل حق بالمعنى الذي يلزم القول به، لولاهما لم يلزم ذلك؛ فيكون المعروف بالعقل وما يوجبه ضرورة ذلك مدفوعاً بالجهل بالحكمة والحادث. ولو جاز ذلك لجاز إنكار الأمر.
Then the proof according to us from the way of the Qur'an for the necessity of affirming the creation of acts is His statement: 'And conceal your speech or publicize it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Acquainted?' [Al-Mulk 13-14]. For if He, exalted be His praise, were not the Creator of what is spoken aloud and what is concealed, He would not have argued by it for His knowledge. And the possibility of ignorance is known from other than the one who does it. So if there is no meaning in arguing by an act of another. Also, Allah the Exalted said: 'It is He who causes you to travel on land and sea' [Yunus 22], and He said in another place: 'And We determined in it journeys; travel therein nights' [Saba' 18], informing that the determination of journeys and causing to travel is His act, and by it travel existed and whoever traveled. And He said: 'And of His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates that you may find tranquility in them, and He placed between you affection and mercy' [Ar-Rum 21], containing the report that the placing of affection and mercy is among His signs, and that your sleep is among His signs and your seeking of His bounty is among His signs. And it is far-fetched that another should originate these signs; for that doer would be more deserving that the sign should belong to him, and they are all acts of the creatures. And He said: 'And We placed in the hearts of those who followed him compassion and mercy' [Al-Hadid 27], and He said: 'Those, He has inscribed faith in their hearts' [Al-Mujadilah 22], and He said: 'And Allah has made for you from the hides of the cattle houses' [An-Nahl 80], and He said: 'And We made their hearts hard' [Al-Ma'idah 13]. And in summary, Allah said: 'Doer of whatever He wills' [Hud 107, etc.], and among the acts of the servants is what He wills, and He has promised to do what He wills. And Allah has condemned those who love to be praised for what they did not do, and He has obliged the believers to praise Him for faith, so it is established that this is by His act. And there is no power except through Allah.

And the principle in this is that the indication of the creation of the act of everyone is greater in His sight than the indication of the creation of the heavens and the earth, in that which is intended to be known by reason of the reality of that: that no one has tested the powers of the substances of the world so as to know the emergence of everything from that and the possibility of creating its like; rather, it is only known by its emergence from the possibility of its like. And it is known that there exist things in other substances such that their substance is prevented from containing that, such as flying, penetrating objects, swimming by the substance, and other things by powers in them. And everyone knows that no creature has management in his act; so it is known by necessity, by what has gone beyond his intention and fallen short of the limit he sets, and was determined by what his capacity cannot bear to determine, so it is known by necessity that the one by which he stood is the one who determined it and brought it forth as He willed. And there is no power except through Allah.

Along with what was not with the Mu'tazila from Allah to His creatures at all except that He brought it into existence after it was non-existent, and that Allah did not cease to exist; and that meaning exists in the act of everyone. However, were it not for the command and prohibition, reason could not bear to remove something from the power of Allah and attribute something to the act of another. And the command and prohibition are in the place of truth in the sense that requires affirming them; without them that would not be required. So what is known by reason and what its necessity necessitates would be repelled by ignorance of wisdom and the contingent. And if that were permissible, then denying the command would be permissible.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage presents Maturidi's scriptural and rational proof for the doctrine that all acts of creatures are created by Allah, a key point against the Mu'tazila who held that humans create their own acts. The passage begins with Quranic evidence: verses where Allah argues from His creation to His knowledge (Al-Mulk 13-14) show that He must be the creator of both hidden and public speech. If He were not, the argument would be invalid. Similarly, verses about causing travel (Yunus 22, Saba' 18) attribute the determination and causing of movement to Allah. Verses about placing affection, mercy, sleep, faith, hardness of heart, and making houses from skins all show that these inner and outer states are acts of Allah — indeed they are called 'signs' (ayat), and it is unlikely that another could originate them. Maturidi then generalizes: Allah is 'Doer of whatever He wills' and among the servants' acts is what He wills. Also, Allah condemns those who want praise for what they did not do, and He obliges believers to praise Him for faith — implying faith is His act.

Then Maturidi adds a rational principle: the evidence for creation of each person's act is even greater than that for creation of the heavens and earth, when considered by reason. No one can know the full capacities of the world's substances to confirm that a creature could create. Rather, we know that things occur beyond a creature's intention and capacity (like flying, penetrating, swimming by nature), showing that the act is determined by another. Thus, by necessity, the one who brings the act into existence is Allah.

Finally, Maturidi engages with Mu'tazila theory: they hold that Allah only brings acts into existence from non-existence (as they consider acts 'things' before existence), but this meaning exists in every act. However, without the revealed command and prohibition, reason would not remove any act from Allah's power and attribute it to the creature. The command and prohibition are true in the sense that they require this attribution; without them, rational knowledge would be overturned by ignorance of wisdom and contingency. Denying this would lead to denying the command itself.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
الضرورة
قوى الجواهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The universe is a greater proof of creation than human acts.
Correction: Maturidi argues that human acts provide even stronger evidence because we directly experience our limits.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why is the indication of creation of each person's act greater than that of the heavens and earth?
A) Because the act is simpler.
B) Because we can directly observe the limits of our power in our acts.
C) Because the heavens and earth are too large.
D) Because the act is not a thing.

Key Takeaway
Our own limitations in executing acts provide direct evidence that they are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan an action but it falls short of your intention, do you recognize that as a sign that your act is determined by Allah, or do you simply see it as your failure? How does this shift your view of your own efforts?
?
The passage says no creature has management in his act. Think of a recent act you felt fully in control of. Was it truly independent? How does admitting Allah's creation of that act change your gratitude or humility?
?
You know you cannot fly or penetrate objects. Why do you still feel you own your actions? What would it take for you to feel the same necessity about Allah's creation of your deeds as you feel about your inability to fly?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on the Attribution of Acts
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila and links act creation to command/prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of the Mu'tazila view that humans create their own acts and his assertion of the necessity of divine command and prohibition.

Core Idea
Without revelation, reason cannot exclude any act from Allah's power.

Maturidi now directly engages with the Mu'tazila. He points out a flaw in their reasoning: they claim that Allah only brings the act into existence after it was non-existent, but this meaning applies to every act. Then he argues that without the divine command and prohibition, reason could not attribute an act to a creature. This shows that the attribution of acts to humans is based on revelation, not pure reason.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila say Allah only brings acts into existence from non-existence, but they think humans then create their own acts.
Maturidi challenges this.
2
Follow Maturidi's argument
Without command/prohibition, reason would not exclude any act from Allah's power. The command/prohibition are necessary for attribution.
This is a key point.
3
See the consequences
If reason alone could attribute acts to creatures, it would be based on ignorance of wisdom. Maturidi warns that denying this leads to denying revelation itself.

According to Maturidi, what prevents reason from attributing an act to a creature?
A) The act's complexity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed something was your own doing without considering that it is ultimately from Allah? Where in your life today can you pause and attribute the act back to Him, not to your own ability?
?

?
If you deny the necessity of divine commands, as the passage warns, you risk denying them altogether. Is there any command of Allah you have denied or minimized? Will you recommit to obeying it, not out of obligation, but because it reveals truth?

Quranic Proof for Capacity of Means
Maturidi cites the zihar verse and the hypocrites' excuse to prove capacity is of means.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the zihar verse and the hypocrites' excuse to prove that the Quranic term 'capacity' refers to capacity of means (external resources) rather than capacity of the act (internal ability).

Core Idea
When the Quran says 'cannot,' it means lacks means, not lacks ability.

Maturidi grounds his division of capacity directly in the Quran. He examines two verses where people are described as unable to do something, and shows that in each case the inability is due to a lack of external resources or circumstances, not a failure of their own power to act. This lesson walks through those two proofs and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the overall argument.
Notice that Maturidi starts with the zihar verse and then gives a second proof from the hypocrites.
2
Understand the zihar verse proof
Maturidi cites Q. 58:4 about expiation for zihar. He argues that 'whoever cannot find a slave' means cannot find the means (a slave to free), not that one lacks the power to fast two months. The capacity to fast persists over two months, so the inability must be about the means.
3
Understand the hypocrites analogy
The hypocrites in Q. 9:42 excused themselves from jihad saying 'if we were able'. They meant illness or lack of wealth (means), not that they lacked the power to act. Allah rebuked them for lying because they actually had the means.
This shows that even when people lie about incapacity, they refer to means, not power.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal conclusion
Ask yourself: Why does this matter? It shows that the Quran consistently uses 'capacity' to mean capacity of external causes and circumstances, which supports Maturidi's division of capacity into two types.
This connects to the larger debate about human agency and divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدلالة على قسمة الاستطاعتين قول الله تعالى : فمن لم يستطع فإطعام ستين مسكينا . ثم الدلالة على أن الاستطاعة استطاعة الأسباب والأحوال لا استطاعة الفعل وجوه. أحدها أن قوله : فمن لم يستطع إنما هو صوم شهرين ولا أحد يعلم أن قدرة الفعل لا تَرده تلك المدة، ثبت أن المراد ذلك استطاعة الوجود ومثله أهل النفاق، لم يكونوا يعلمون الاستطاعة التي لديها الأفعال، وإنما أرادوا بذلك المرض أو فقد المال على ما بيننا الله تعالى بقوله : ليس على الضعفاء إلى قوله إنما السبيل على الذين يستأذنونك وهم أغنياء الآية .
Then the indication of the division of the two capacities is Allah's saying: 'Then whoever cannot [find a slave], let him fast two consecutive months' (Q. 58:4). Then the indication that the capacity is the capacity of causes and circumstances, not the capacity of the act, is [through] aspects. One of them is that His saying 'whoever cannot' refers to fasting of two months, and no one knows that the capacity of the act does not last that period, so it is established that what is meant by that is the capacity of existence. And similarly the people of hypocrisy; they did not know the capacity that is with actions, but rather they meant by that illness or lack of wealth, as Allah explained to us in His saying: 'There is no blame on the weak...' up to His saying '...the blame is only upon those who ask permission of you while they are rich.' (Q. 9:91-93).
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural proof for the distinction between the two types of capacity. Maturidi first cites the verse from Surah al-Mujadila (58:4) which speaks of 'whoever cannot find [a slave to free]' and then prescribes fasting. He argues that the capacity mentioned here cannot be the capacity of the act (qudrat al-fi'l) because that capacity is not known to persist for the duration of two months of fasting. Rather, it is the capacity of the means or circumstances (istita'at al-asbab wa al-ahwal) that allows one to fulfill the obligation. He then draws an analogy to the hypocrites mentioned in Surah al-Tawba (9:42, 91-93) who excused themselves from jihad by saying 'if we were able, we would have gone out with you.' They did not mean that they lacked the capacity of the act itself (which would be a technical and obscure concept), but rather they meant illness or lack of wealth, i.e., the capacity of means. Allah rebuked them for lying because they actually had the means but pretended they did not. Thus, the Quranic usage of 'capacity' consistently refers to the capacity of means, not the capacity of the act.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
استطاعة الوجود
أهل النفاق
آية الظهار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Quranic verses refer to the capacity of the act itself (internal power to perform).
Correction: Maturidi shows that in both the zihar verse and the hypocrites' excuse, the inability is due to lack of external means (slave, wealth, health), not lack of the power to act.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Maturidi use as the primary evidence for the division of capacity?
A) Q. 58:4
B) Q. 9:42
C) Q. 9:91
D) Q. 2:286

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the Quran consistently uses 'capacity' to mean capacity of means, not capacity of the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I can't' regarding a religious obligation like praying on time or giving charity, are you truly lacking the means, or are you making an excuse like the hypocrites? How often do you examine your own heart before Allah before uttering those words? What one excuse will you stop using this week?
?
The hypocrites had the means but claimed they didn't. Allah exposed their lie. If your inner thoughts were exposed to others, would your 'I can't' statements be proven genuine or false? Are there areas where you have the means (time, health, wealth) but pretend you don't? Commit to one action you've been avoiding due to a false sense of inability.
?
Maturidi shows that the Quran's meaning of capacity is about having the means, not about having the innate ability. How does this change your view of responsibilities you've labeled as 'too hard'? Is there a duty you've neglected because you thought you lacked ability, when in fact you have the means? What will you do about it starting today?

Answer to the Objection from the Verse 'Aw La Yastati' An Yumilla
Maturidi answers an objection based on the verse 'Aw la yastati' an yumilla huwa'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi responds to an objection from a Quranic verse about dictation, distinguishing between incapacity due to lack of power and lack of skill.

Core Idea
Not every inability is a lack of power; some are a lack of knowledge.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses an opponent's argument based on Quran 2:282, which mentions someone unable to dictate. The opponent likely used this to claim that power (istita'a) can be absent before an action, implying it is separate from the action. Maturidi offers two counterpoints: the verse may refer to not knowing how to dictate (i.e., lacking skill), and he reiterates the principle that complete power does not precede the action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the two distinct parts of Maturidi's response.
The passage is dense, so take your time.
2
Identify the two responses
Notice that Maturidi first says the answer has already been given, then offers an alternative interpretation of the verse. Find where he shifts.
The phrase 'ma' ihtimalihi li-ma'na la yuhsin' signals the alternative.
3
Understand 'capability of incapacity'
Maturidi says the verse also indicates 'the capability of incapacity'. Reflect on how this paradoxical phrase highlights that the inability here is not a lack of power but a lack of skill.
4
Connect to the principle of power
Maturidi reiterates that complete power does not precede the beginning of an action. Connect this to the broader Maturidi view that power is simultaneous with the action.
This supports the idea that power cannot exist before the action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتجاجه بقوله: «أو لا يستطيع أن يُمل هو»، فجوابه كاما سلف بيانه، مع احتماله لمعنى لا يحسن، وهو استطاعة العجز أيضا. دليل ذلك ما بينا أن قدرة التمام لا تكون قبل الابتداء، وقد أضيف إليه الكل. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And his argument by His saying: 'Or one who is unable to dictate, let his guardian dictate justly.' Its answer is as previously explained, with its possibility of meaning 'does not know well', and it is also the capability of incapacity. The proof of that is what we have explained that complete power is not before beginning, and the whole has been attributed to him. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection based on Quran 2:282: 'or if he is unable to dictate, let his guardian dictate justly.' The opponent (al-Ka'bi) likely used this to argue that if someone cannot dictate (due to incapacity), then power is separate. Maturidi responds that the answer has already been given. He adds that the verse can also be interpreted to mean 'does not know how to dictate', i.e., it refers to skill, not the power to act. Moreover, he reiterates that complete power does not precede the beginning of the action; rather, it is simultaneous. The phrase 'the whole has been attributed to him' refers to the fact that the entire action is ascribed to the agent at the moment of its occurrence.

Key Terms
استطاعة (istita'a)
قدرة (qudra)
عجز ('ajz)
إملاء (imla')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'aw la yastati' an yumilla' proves that power (istita'a) can be absent before an action, implying it is separate from the action.
Correction: Maturidi shows the verse can refer to lack of skill, not lack of power. His principle is that complete power is simultaneous with action, not separate.

Checkpoint

A) It means he lacks the physical ability to speak.
B) It means he does not know how to dictate well.
C) It means he lacks the legal capacity.
D) It means he has no power over his actions.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi counters that the verse can be read as referring to lack of skill, not lack of power, supporting his view that power is simultaneous with action.

Second and Third Interpretations of the Verse on Despair
Maturidi explains the second and third meanings of the verse about messengers' despair.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two rational explanations for why disbelievers called messengers liars despite clear signs: mistaken attribution of God's respite as approval, and mockery of believers' reliance on God's will.

Core Idea
Respite does not imply approval, and mockery does not negate truth.

This lesson continues Maturidi's tafsir of the verse on messengers' despair. Having already presented one interpretation, he now offers two more: one rooted in the disbelievers’ misreading of divine patience, the other in their mocking dismissal of believers’ faith in God's will. Both interpretations protect the honor of the messengers and clarify the nature of divine testing.

Guided Path
1
Understand the second interpretation
Read the explanation of how disbelievers misconstrued God's respite as approval, leading them to think the messengers were lying.
Notice the comparison with the people of the Sabbath.
2
Examine the third interpretation
Understand how disbelievers mock believers who affirm that everything is by God's will, using examples like the man who says 'If I die, I will be brought out alive.'
Consider how mockery does not make a true statement false.
3
Connect to the verse's conclusion
See how the end of the verse (6:149) supports these interpretations, emphasizing that God's conclusive argument is decisive.
Reflect on why no other interpretation is plausible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني أنهم لَمّا أُوعِدوا في ذلك قد أُمهلوا، فلما أمهلوا ظنوا كذب الرسل وحسبوا أن ذلك مما لله فيه الرضا، وإلا لم يكن يمهلهم، وكذلك ظن أصحاب السبت . وذلك كقوله [ تعالى ]: حتى إذا استيأس الرسل ، الآية . والثالث أن يكونوا قالوه على الاستهزاء بالمؤمنين بما يدعون أن كل شيء بمشيئة الله، كقول الإنسان: أإذا ما مت لسوف أخرج حيّا ، إنه قال ذلك على الاستهزاء بالمؤمنين، وإن كان ذلك حقاً؛ وكذلك قول المنافقين: نشهد إنك لرسول الله ، ولكن ذلك لما كان الهزوء طعنوا به، فمثله الأول. والله أعلم . [و] أيّد ذلك آخر الآية : قل فلله الحجة البالغة فلو شاء لهداكم أجمعين [الأنعام ١٤٩/٦] ، وغير ذلك، ولا يحتمل لما مر بيانه.
And the second: that when they were threatened in that, they were given respite, and when they were given respite they thought the messengers were lying and supposed that this is something with which God is pleased, otherwise He would not have given them respite. Similarly, the people of the Sabbath thought that. That is like His saying [Exalted]: 'Until when the messengers despaired,' the verse. And the third: that they said it in mockery of the believers, because they claim that everything is by God's will, like the saying of a man: 'If I die, I will surely be brought out alive.' He said that in mockery of the believers, even if it is true. Similarly, the saying of the hypocrites: 'We bear witness that you are the Messenger of God.' But because it was mockery, they attacked with it, so it is like the first. And God knows best. And that is supported by the end of the verse: 'Say, to God belongs the conclusive argument; if He willed, He would have guided you all.' [6:149] And other than that, and it is not possible [otherwise] due to what has been explained.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage presents two of the three interpretations (the second and third) of the verse about the messengers' despair. The second interpretation is that the disbelievers, when threatened with punishment, were given respite; they mistakenly thought this respite indicated God's approval, leading them to call the messengers liars. The author compares them to the people of the Sabbath who similarly misinterpreted God's patience. He cites the verse 'Until when the messengers despaired' as support. The third interpretation is that the disbelievers said these things in mockery of the believers, who affirm that everything is by God's will. Examples include the man who says 'If I die, I will surely be brought out alive'—a statement that is true in itself but is uttered derisively—and the hypocrites who say 'We bear witness that you are the Messenger of God' mockingly. The author notes that such mockery is akin to the first interpretation. He then affirms that the end of the verse (6:149) supports these interpretations, as it states that the conclusive argument belongs to God; if He willed, He would have guided all. The passage concludes by stating that no other interpretation is plausible given what has been explained earlier.

Key Terms
إمهال (respite)
استهزاء (mockery)
مشيئة الله (God's will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if God gives respite to disbelievers, He is pleased with their actions.
Correction: The passage clarifies that respite is a test, not a sign of approval. The disbelievers' assumption was mistaken, as shown by the comparison to the people of the Sabbath and the support of the verse.

Checkpoint
What is the second interpretation of why the disbelievers thought the messengers were lying?
A) They were mocking the believers.
B) They were given respite and thought God was pleased with them.
C) They were forced to disbelieve.
D) They did not understand the message.

Key Takeaway
God's respite is a test, not approval, and mockery does not affect the truth of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see people who openly mock Islam yet seem to prosper, does your faith waver? How does Maturidi's explanation of respite as a test—not approval—demand that you trust God's wisdom instead of your own judgment?
?
Have you ever uttered a statement of faith insincerely, perhaps to fit in or avoid conflict? The hypocrites said 'We bear witness you are the Messenger of God' but meant it as mockery. Before your next testimony, will you examine your heart to ensure your words are not empty?
?
The disbelievers mocked the truth of resurrection because of the believers who affirmed it. Are there truths you know but are too afraid to affirm openly because of how others might react? This lesson shows that mockery does not change truth. What will you do this week to stand by a truth you have been hiding?

Maturidi's Definition of Hypocrisy and Its Application to Major Sinners
Maturidi defines nifaq using Quran and hadith and applies it to major sinners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's definition of hypocrisy (nifaq) and how he uses Quran and hadith to argue that major sinners are hypocrites.

Core Idea
Hypocrisy is when your actions contradict your words of faith.

Imam Maturidi presents a sharp definition of hypocrisy (nifaq) that goes beyond hiding disbelief. He argues that major sinners who violate Allah's limits are hypocrites, because their actions contradict their verbal faith. In this passage, he grounds his argument in the Quran and a famous hadith about the signs of hypocrisy.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's definition of nifaq
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Maturidi defines hypocrisy as contradicting what one says with one's tongue through one's actions.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Note the two Quranic verses Maturidi cites. The first says Allah will distinguish believers from hypocrites; the second implies testing to reveal truthfulness. Consider how these support his definition.
3
Analyze the prophetic hadith
The hadith lists three signs of hypocrisy: lying, breaking promises, and betraying trusts. Maturidi asserts that these are visible in the major sinner.
4
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that major sinners display the signs of hypocrisy, so they cannot be considered true believers. This is a polemical point against those who would place such sinners in a middle category.
This connects to debates about faith and works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن حقق له اسم النفاق فلمخالفة ما أعطى بلسانه من الإيمان وتعاهد حدوده وحفظ حدود الله ما ظهر بأفعاله، وبذلك قال الله تعالى: وليعلمن الله الذين آمنوا وليعلمن المنافقين [العنكبوت، ١١/٢٩]، وقال: ألم. أحسب الناس أن يُتركوا الآية، أخبر بأن خالدا فيها وغضب
بيان ما أعطته الألسن من الصدق والكذب بالمحنة. وكذا روى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: ثلاث من كن فيه فهو منافق من إذا حدث كذب، وإذا وعد أخلف، وإذا اؤتمن خان. فقد ظهر له ذلك كله من مرتكب الكبيرة. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And whoever has the name 'hypocrisy' (nifaq) verified for him, it is due to contradicting what he gave with his tongue of faith (iman) and violating its limits and not preserving the limits of Allah in what appears with his actions. And by that Allah said: 'And Allah will surely know those who believe and will surely know the hypocrites' [al-Ankabut 29:11]. And He said: 'Alif Lam Meem. Do the people think that they will be left...' the verse, informing that he who is...? And anger... Clarifying what the tongues give of truth and falsehood through trial. And likewise it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'Three things, whoever has them is a hypocrite: when he speaks he lies, when he promises he breaks, and when he is entrusted he betrays.' So all of that has appeared from the committer of major sins (murtakib al-kabirah). And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage defines hypocrisy (nifaq) as a contradiction between one's verbal confession of faith and one's actions with regard to the limits set by Allah. Maturidi cites two Quranic verses: one stating that Allah will distinguish the believers from the hypocrites, and another from Surat al-Ankabut that implies testing to reveal truthfulness and falsehood. He then brings a prophetic hadith listing three signs of hypocrisy: lying, breaking promises, and betraying trusts. Maturidi concludes that these signs are manifestly found in the committer of major sins, implying that such a person is a hypocrite. This serves as an argument against the Mu'tazila who refuse to call such sinners either believers or disbelievers, but instead label them as fasiq. By showing that major sins are signs of hypocrisy, Maturidi strengthens the case that the committer of major sins is not a true believer.

مرتكب الكبيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Hypocrisy only applies to those who hide disbelief while outwardly appearing Muslim.
Correction: Maturidi expands hypocrisy to include those whose actions contradict their faith, such as major sinners who violate Allah's limits.

The Mu'tazila Argument and the First Interpretation (Intercession)
Maturidi presents the Mu'tazila argument and the first interpretation of the key verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi introduces the Mu'tazila argument based on the verse and offers the first interpretation that the 'not disgracing' refers to intercession, not to immunity from punishment.

Core Idea
The verse does not promise immunity; it promises intercession.

In this passage, Maturidi begins his refutation of the Mu'tazila who claim that a committer of major sins cannot be a believer because believers are not punished. He cites the verse about the Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and the believers. Then he states that the verse has multiple aspects, beginning with the first: intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the Mu'tazila claim and Maturidi's response.
Notice the structure: claim, then first interpretation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
The Mu'tazila argue that the verse shows a believer is not punished, so a major sinner cannot be a believer.
They infer from 'la yukhzi' that there is no punishment.
3
Analyze the first interpretation
Maturidi explains that 'la yukhzi' refers to intercession, not to absence of punishment. Punishment can still occur, but intercession saves from disgrace.
This reinterprets the verse to allow for temporary punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج بالآية التي فيها ﴿ يوم لا يخزى الله النبي والذين آمنوا معه ﴾ في صاحب الكبيرة أنه لو كان مؤمناً لكان لا يعذب ولا يوعد عليه. والآية ترجع إلى وجوه. أحدها أن لا يخزيه عن شفاعة رسول الله، بل يشفعه فيه وينجيه بها. والثاني أن يكون ذلك عندما يقول لهم تواهبوا مظالمكم، وعلى معذرتكم. والثالث أن يكون لا يخزيهم خزى الكفرة من الخلود في النار؛ إذ هو أنواع كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ ليس لهم طعام إلا من ضريع ﴾ [الغاشية: ٦/٨٨]، وقال في موضع ﴿ فليس له اليوم ههنا حميم ولا طعام إلا من غسلين ﴾ [الحاقة: ٣٥-٣٦/٦٩] على اختلاف الدركات فمثله على اختلاف الأوقات. ويحتمل لا يخزى أي لا يفضحه فيهتك ستره، وذلك كذلك في كل مؤمن. ثم الذي ينقض على المعتزلة ابتداء الآية وهو قوله: ﴿ يا أيها الذين آمنوا توبوا إلى الله توبة نصوحاً ﴾ [التحريم: ٨/٦٦] ألزمهم التوبة وجعلها شرطاً للمغفرة، على إبقاء اسم الإيمان لهم، والصغائر مغفورة باجتناب الكبائر على قولهم. ثبت أن الآية في أصحاب الكبائر، وقد بقى لهم اسم الإيمان. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then he argued by the verse which contains: 'The Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him' concerning the committer of a major sin, that if he were a believer, he would not be punished nor threatened with punishment. But the verse has aspects. One aspect: that He will not disgrace him by the intercession of the Messenger of God, but rather He will grant him intercession and save him by it. The second: that it will be when He says to them: 'Forgive one another your wrongs, and accept one another's excuses.' The third: that He will not disgrace them with the disgrace of the disbelievers of eternal abidance in the Fire; for it is of various kinds, as God Almighty said: 'For them no food except from darī' (thorny plant)' [al-Ghashiyya: 6/88], and He said elsewhere: 'So for him here today no intimate friend, nor any food except from ghislin (filth)' [al-Haqqa: 35-36/69] according to differences in degrees, and likewise according to differences in times. And it is possible that 'la yukhzi' means that He will not put him to shame by uncovering his secret, and that applies to every believer. Then what refutes the Mu'tazila from the beginning of the verse is His saying: 'O you who have believed, repent to God a sincere repentance' [al-Tahrim: 8/66]. He obligated repentance upon them and made it a condition for forgiveness, while preserving the name of faith for them, and minor sins are forgiven by avoiding major sins according to their claim. So it is established that the verse is about the committers of major sins, and the name of faith remained for them. There is no power except in God.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the Mu'tazila argument that a committer of major sin cannot be a believer because a believer would not be punished. The author (likely Maturidi) offers three interpretations of the key verse 'Yawma la yukhzi Allah al-nabi wa alladhina amanu' to show it does not support their position. First interpretation: the 'not disgracing' refers to the intercession of the Prophet, saving the sinner, not to absence of punishment. Second interpretation: the 'not disgracing' occurs on the Day when God tells people to forgive each other their wrongs and accept excuses, meaning that the disgrace is removed through mutual forgiveness, not that no sin occurred. Third interpretation: 'not disgracing' means not being eternally disgraced like the disbelievers, since punishments in Hell have various degrees and times—thus a believer may be punished temporarily but not eternally. The author adds a fourth possible meaning: 'not disgracing' means not exposing one's secrets publicly, which applies to all believers. He then strengthens the refutation by pointing to the very next verse in Sura al-Tahrim (8:66) which commands believers to repent sincerely, addressing them as 'believers' and making repentance a condition for forgiveness, thereby proving that the addressees still had the name of faith despite their sins. This shows the verse itself preserves the name of faith for those who commit major sins.

Key Terms
آية
شفاعة
خزي
كبيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse means believers will never face any punishment or disgrace.
Correction: Maturidi shows it means they will be saved by intercession, not that they are immune.

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation, how is a believer saved from disgrace on that Day?
A) By his own good deeds
B) By the intercession of the Prophet
C) By not committing sins
D) By avoiding major sins

Key Takeaway
The first interpretation shows that the verse's promise of not being disgraced refers to salvation through intercession, not to freedom from punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly assume that your good deeds or your identity as a Muslim will save you from punishment, or are you genuinely hopeful in the Prophet's intercession while fearful of your sins? How does this verse's reinterpretation affect your daily struggle with sin?
?
If you knew that your salvation depends entirely on intercession, not on your record of deeds, would that make you more reliant on seeking the Prophet's intercession? In what concrete way can you increase your connection to the Prophet so that his intercession might include you?
?
The Mu'tazila thought that a believer cannot be punished. Do you live as though you cannot be punished because you 'believe'? How does this lesson challenge your sense of security and call you to repentance?

Further Interpretations: Mutual Forgiveness, Degrees of Punishment, and Concealment
Maturidi explains the second and third aspects of the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second and third interpretations of the verse, along with a fourth possibility, all of which allow for a believer to experience temporary punishment.

Core Idea
The verse allows for temporary punishment; believers are not subject to eternal disgrace like disbelievers.

Maturidi continues his exegesis by offering two more explicit aspects of the verse. The second aspect relates to mutual forgiveness among believers on that Day, and the third aspect emphasizes that believers will not be disgraced with the eternal disgrace of disbelievers—they may face temporary punishment. He then adds a fourth possibility: that 'not disgracing' means not exposing one's secrets publicly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second and third interpretations.
Also note the fourth possibility.
2
Understand the second interpretation
The 'not disgracing' is realized when God tells believers to forgive each other's wrongs. This implies that wrongs exist but are forgiven.
No contradiction with punishment.
3
Understand the third interpretation
Believers are not disgraced like disbelievers who are eternally in Hell. Their punishment, if any, is limited in degree and time.
Refers to verses about varying foods in Hell.
4
Note the fourth possibility
God does not expose the believer's secrets publicly. This applies to all believers.
Another way to understand 'not disgracing'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج بالآية التي فيها ﴿ يوم لا يخزى الله النبي والذين آمنوا معه ﴾ في صاحب الكبيرة أنه لو كان مؤمناً لكان لا يعذب ولا يوعد عليه. والآية ترجع إلى وجوه. أحدها أن لا يخزيه عن شفاعة رسول الله، بل يشفعه فيه وينجيه بها. والثاني أن يكون ذلك عندما يقول لهم تواهبوا مظالمكم، وعلى معذرتكم. والثالث أن يكون لا يخزيهم خزى الكفرة من الخلود في النار؛ إذ هو أنواع كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ ليس لهم طعام إلا من ضريع ﴾ [الغاشية: ٦/٨٨]، وقال في موضع ﴿ فليس له اليوم ههنا حميم ولا طعام إلا من غسلين ﴾ [الحاقة: ٣٥-٣٦/٦٩] على اختلاف الدركات فمثله على اختلاف الأوقات. ويحتمل لا يخزى أي لا يفضحه فيهتك ستره، وذلك كذلك في كل مؤمن. ثم الذي ينقض على المعتزلة ابتداء الآية وهو قوله: ﴿ يا أيها الذين آمنوا توبوا إلى الله توبة نصوحاً ﴾ [التحريم: ٨/٦٦] ألزمهم التوبة وجعلها شرطاً للمغفرة، على إبقاء اسم الإيمان لهم، والصغائر مغفورة باجتناب الكبائر على قولهم. ثبت أن الآية في أصحاب الكبائر، وقد بقى لهم اسم الإيمان. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then he argued by the verse which contains: 'The Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him' concerning the committer of a major sin, that if he were a believer, he would not be punished nor threatened with punishment. But the verse has aspects. One aspect: that He will not disgrace him by the intercession of the Messenger of God, but rather He will grant him intercession and save him by it. The second: that it will be when He says to them: 'Forgive one another your wrongs, and accept one another's excuses.' The third: that He will not disgrace them with the disgrace of the disbelievers of eternal abidance in the Fire; for it is of various kinds, as God Almighty said: 'For them no food except from darī' (thorny plant)' [al-Ghashiyya: 6/88], and He said elsewhere: 'So for him here today no intimate friend, nor any food except from ghislin (filth)' [al-Haqqa: 35-36/69] according to differences in degrees, and likewise according to differences in times. And it is possible that 'la yukhzi' means that He will not put him to shame by uncovering his secret, and that applies to every believer. Then what refutes the Mu'tazila from the beginning of the verse is His saying: 'O you who have believed, repent to God a sincere repentance' [al-Tahrim: 8/66]. He obligated repentance upon them and made it a condition for forgiveness, while preserving the name of faith for them, and minor sins are forgiven by avoiding major sins according to their claim. So it is established that the verse is about the committers of major sins, and the name of faith remained for them. There is no power except in God.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage presents a refutation of the Mu'tazila argument that a committer of major sin cannot be a believer because a believer would not be punished. The author (likely Maturidi) offers three interpretations of the key verse 'Yawma la yukhzi Allah al-nabi wa alladhina amanu' to show it does not support their position. First interpretation: the 'not disgracing' refers to the intercession of the Prophet, saving the sinner, not to absence of punishment. Second interpretation: the 'not disgracing' occurs on the Day when God tells people to forgive each other their wrongs and accept excuses, meaning that the disgrace is removed through mutual forgiveness, not that no sin occurred. Third interpretation: 'not disgracing' means not being eternally disgraced like the disbelievers, since punishments in Hell have various degrees and times—thus a believer may be punished temporarily but not eternally. The author adds a fourth possible meaning: 'not disgracing' means not exposing one's secrets publicly, which applies to all believers. He then strengthens the refutation by pointing to the very next verse in Sura al-Tahrim (8:66) which commands believers to repent sincerely, addressing them as 'believers' and making repentance a condition for forgiveness, thereby proving that the addressees still had the name of faith despite their sins. This shows the verse itself preserves the name of faith for those who commit major sins.

Key Terms
تواهب
مظالم
معذرت
خزي
خلود
دركات
ضريع
غسلين
فضح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believers will never face any punishment at all on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: Maturidi explains that believers may face temporary punishment but not the eternal disgrace of disbelievers.

Checkpoint
What does the third interpretation of 'la yukhzi' emphasize?
A) That believers will not be punished at all
B) That believers will not be disgraced like disbelievers eternally
C) That believers will be punished exactly like disbelievers
D) That only prophets are saved from disgrace

Key Takeaway
The second and third interpretations show that the verse can allow for temporary punishment, as it distinguishes the disgrace of believers from the eternal disgrace of disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that on the Day of Judgment God will command mutual forgiveness among believers, is there someone you have wronged or who has wronged you that you need to forgive today? What concrete step will you take this week to release that grudge?
?
The passage teaches that believers may still be punished temporarily, but their secret sins will not be exposed. What hidden habit or sin are you most afraid of being exposed? Are you truly repentant, or merely afraid of shame? How will you turn to Allah for forgiveness before that Day?
?
If punishment is a real possibility even for believers, how does that change the way you approach your small, private sins? Will you continue to treat them as insignificant, or will you begin to take them seriously and seek forgiveness now?

The Strongest Refutation: Sura al-Tahrim Preserves the Name of Faith for Sinners
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila using the command to repent in Sura al-Tahrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the command to repent to believers in Sura al-Tahrim as a decisive refutation of the Mu'tazila claim.

Core Idea
The Quran addresses sinners as 'believers' and commands repentance, proving faith remains despite major sins.

After discussing the multiple interpretations of the first verse, Maturidi presents a more direct refutation. He points to the beginning of the same sura (al-Tahrim) where Allah commands the believers to repent sincerely, while still addressing them as 'O you who have believed.' This shows that the name of faith remains even for those who need to repent from major sins, contradicting the Mu'tazila who say major sinners lose faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the refutation from Sura al-Tahrim.
Pay attention to the address 'O you who have believed'.
2
Understand the argument
Allah commands believers to repent, implying they have sinned but still retain the name of faith.
Repentance is for major sins.
3
See the refutation's strength
This directly contradicts the Mu'tazila claim that major sin removes faith. The Quran itself preserves the name of faith for sinners.
Thus the verse supports the Sunni position.

Refuting al-Ka'bi on Repentance from a Forgiven Sin
Maturidi refutes al-Ka'bi's two interpretations of Q. 66:8 regarding repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi rejects al-Ka'bi's claim that repentance can be performed for a forgiven sin, and how this relates to gratitude and the concept of faith.

Core Idea
Repentance requires regret, impossible for a forgiven sin; commanding it implies ingratitude.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi engages with al-Ka'bi's creative interpretation of the repentance verse (Q. 66:8). Al-Ka'bi argued that repentance can be from a minor sin even if forgiven, or purely as an act of worship like saying 'la ilaha illa Allah'. Maturidi dismantles these arguments, showing they misunderstand the nature of repentance and lead to ingratitude towards Allah's forgiveness. Let's follow his logical refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ka'bi's two arguments
Identify the two ways al-Ka'bi claimed repentance can be valid: from a forgiven minor sin, and as a worship act like tahlil.
Al-Ka'bi tried to avoid the implication that the sin remains.
2
Maturidi's first counterargument
Notice how Maturidi defines repentance as 'return and regret', and why this cannot apply to a sin that is already forgiven and not subject to punishment.
3
Maturidi's second counterargument
Understand the point about gratitude: if a sin is forgiven, the proper response is praise and thanks, not repentance, which implies the sin is still there.
This ties repentance to ingratitude (kufran al-ni'am).
4
Maturidi's third counterargument
See how the verse itself ('perhaps your Lord will remove your sins') shows that removal depends on repentance, proving the sin remains, yet the person is still a believer.
This preserves the name of faith for the sinner.
5
Distinguish between tahlil and repentance
Learn why tahlil can be repeated as worship (renewal of faith) while repentance is specific to sin, and commanding it for a forgiven sin is impermissible.
The prohibition of supplicating that Allah be unjust is analogous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نذكر ما ذكر الكعبي فيما احتج عليه من القرآن من الحيل المستبعدة ليصرف عن نفسه وأتباعه اسم الإيمان ويوجب الإياس عن روح الله والاختيار لعدواته بكبيرة، كأنه به يحصل على نفع في الدنيا وحمد في الدين. ولا قوة إلا بالله . فقال لمن احتج عليه بقوله : يا أيها الذين آمنوا توبوا إلى الله توبة نصوحا ] [التحريم، ٨/٦٦] الآية ، والتوبة لا تكون إلا عن ذنب بوجهين . أحدهما هو التوبة عن الصغيرة وإن كانت مغفورة ؛ والثاني على التعبد كتكرار التهليل وكدعاء الملائكة بقوله: فاغفر للذين تابوا الآية .
نقول له : الوجه الأول دل على جهله بمعنى التوبة، إذ هي الرجوع والندم، ومحال ذلك عما ليس عليه، وهو مغفور له لا يجوز عليه التعذيب والثاني أن حق الله عليه إذا غفر له الحمد له والشكر على العفو وفي التوبة كفران ذلك، لأنه يوهم بقاءه بالتوبة. والثالث أنه قال: عسى ربكم أن يكفر عنكم سيئاتكم ﴾ [التحريم ، ٨/٦٦] الآية ، فجعله موقوفا على ما يكفره بالتوبة، ثبت أن الذنب باق وهو لم يزل [ مستحقاً ] اسم الإيمان. والله أعلم. والتهليل له في كل وقت حكم التجديد ، لأن حقيقة الأفعال أن لا يبقى، والتوبة يكون عن ذنب، ولا ذنب. وبعد، فإنه يجوز الأمر بالتهليل على التعبد ولا يجوز بالتوبة والاستغفار عن ذنب معفو مغفور ، لما فيه إيهام أنه ليس بمغفور . وذلك كفران النعم، وغير جائز ذلك، كما لا يجوز الدعاء بأن لا يجور ولا يظلم. ودعاء الملائكة لما قد يكون لمن ذكر ذنوب غير
Then we mention what al-Ka'bi mentioned in his argument from the Quran [consisting] of far-fetched ruses to turn away the name of faith from himself and his followers and to necessitate despair of Allah's mercy and preference for His enmity by a major sin, as if thereby he achieves worldly benefit and religious praise. There is no power except with Allah. So he said to one who argued against him using His statement: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance' [Q. 66:8] — the verse — and repentance is only from a sin in two ways: one of them is repentance from a minor sin even if it is forgiven; and the second is as an act of worship, like repeating the tahlil (saying 'la ilaha illa Allah') and like the supplication of the angels in His statement: 'So forgive those who repent' [Q. 40:7] — the verse.
We say to him: The first way indicates his ignorance of the meaning of repentance, for it is returning and regret, and this is impossible regarding what one is not upon, and he is forgiven and not subject to punishment. The second [is that] Allah's right upon him, when He forgives him, is to praise Him and thank Him for pardon, while in repentance there is ingratitude for that, because it implies remaining [in need of] repentance. The third [point] is that he said: 'Perhaps your Lord will remove from you your sins' [Q. 66:8] — the verse — and He made it dependent on what He removes by repentance; it is established that the sin remains, and [the person] has not ceased to deserve the name of faith. And Allah knows best. And the tahlil has the ruling of renewal at every time, because the reality of actions is that they do not endure, and repentance is from a sin, and there is no sin. Moreover, it is permissible to command tahlil as an act of worship, but it is not permissible [to command] repentance and seeking forgiveness from a sin that is pardoned and forgiven, because it implies that it is not forgiven. That is ingratitude for blessings, and it is not permissible, just as it is not permissible to supplicate that He not be unjust or oppress. And the supplication of the angels may be for those who have mentioned sins that are not
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of al-Ka'bi's interpretation of the repentance verse (Q. 66:8). The author begins by condemning al-Ka'bi's motives, then presents al-Ka'bi's two arguments: first, that repentance can be from a minor sin even if forgiven; second, that repentance can be an act of worship like tahlil. The author then offers three counterarguments: (1) Repentance means returning and regret, which is impossible when one is not actually guilty; a forgiven person has no sin to regret. (2) If a sin is forgiven, gratitude is due to Allah; performing repentance implies ingratitude by suggesting the sin still needs to be removed. (3) The verse 'Perhaps your Lord will remove from you your sins' shows that removal is conditional on repentance, proving the sin remains; yet the person is still called a believer. The author also argues that tahlil can be repeated as an act of worship because it is a renewal of faith, while repentance is specific to sin; commanding repentance for a forgiven sin is improper because it implies the sin is not forgiven, which is ingratitude. The passage ends mid-sentence discussing the angels' supplication.

Key Terms
توبة
تهليل
ذنب
مغفورة
كفران النعم
استغفار
كعبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That repentance can be performed for a sin that is already forgiven, either as an act of worship or to acknowledge the sin even if forgiven.
Correction: Repentance requires regret, which is impossible if the sin is forgiven and carries no punishment. Moreover, performing repentance for a forgiven sin implies ingratitude by suggesting the forgiveness is incomplete.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi reject al-Ka'bi's claim that repentance can be from a forgiven minor sin?
A) Because repentance requires regret, which is impossible for a sin that is already forgiven.
B) Because repentance is only for major sins.
C) Because the verse commands repentance for unbelief.
D) Because al-Ka'bi misinterpreted the angels' supplication.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that repentance is only valid for an actual sin; commanding it for a forgiven sin is both impossible and an act of ingratitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever continued to feel guilty over a sin you have sincerely repented from and believed Allah has forgiven? How does this lesson challenge you to accept His forgiveness fully and replace guilt with gratitude?
?
The author warns that repenting from a forgiven sin is ingratitude. In your daily life, do you spend more time dwelling on past mistakes or thanking Allah for His mercy? What concrete step can you take today to shift from regret to thankfulness?
?
If repentance is only for actual sins, what sin in your life right now are you avoiding confronting because it is easier to dwell on the past? What would sincere tawba from that sin look like for you?

Preventive Rebuke in Quran 61:2
Maturidi interprets Quran 61:2 as a preventive rebuke, not a criticism of past action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's interpretation of Quran 61:2 as a preventive warning rather than a criticism of past action.

Core Idea
The Quranic rebuke is a shield, not a sword.

This verse is often cited against hypocrisy, but Maturidi offers a nuanced reading: the rebuke is meant to prevent a sin that has not yet occurred. He illustrates this with the example of a person warning another against following misguiders. This lesson unpacks that interpretation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Carefully read the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice how Maturidi introduces his interpretation with 'except that this is regarding something that has not been done.'
The Arabic uses the phrase 'لم تقولون ما لا تفعلون' which is the verse being explained.
2
Understand the preventive context
Focus on Maturidi's point: the rebuke is not for a past failure but for a potential future sin. The example clarifies this: the warning is given so that the person does not commit the evil act.
Contrast this with the common reading that condemns saying something you don't do.
3
Analyze the example
Consider the scenario: someone is being called to an evil matter by misguiders. The speaker says 'Why do you not do...?' as a prohibition, not a question of fact. Ask yourself how this changes the meaning of the verse.
The example is key to Maturidi's tafsir method.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Summarize in your own words why this interpretation matters for understanding Quranic ethics and divine address.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال في قوله : يا أيها الذين آمنوا لم تقولون ما لا تفعلون إلا أن ذا يكون فيما لم يكن فعله، كمن يرى آخر يدعوه بعض الغواة إلى أمر قبيح، فيقول على سبيل النهي : لم تفعل يا أخي ما ينقص دينك ويوجب عليك سخط ربك ? لا أنه فَعَلَه، لكن لئلا يفعله.
Then He said regarding His statement: 'O you who have believed, why do you say what you do not do?' except that this is regarding something that has not been done, like one who sees another being called by some misguiders to an evil matter, so he says by way of prohibition: 'Why do you not do, O my brother, that which diminishes your religion and necessitates upon you the wrath of your Lord?' Not that he has done it, but so that he does not do it.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a verse interpretation. Maturidi explains that the Quranic rebuke in 61:2 is not about saying something you have already failed to do, but about preventing a future wrong action. He gives an example: a person warns another being tempted to sin by saying 'why would you do that which harms your religion?' The point is to stop the sin before it happens, not to scold for a past omission.

Key Terms
لم تقولون ما لا تفعلون
النهي
الغواة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that Quran 61:2 is exclusively rebuking hypocrisy—saying something then not doing it.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the verse can be interpreted as a preventive prohibition against a future evil act, not necessarily a critique of a past failure.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the context of the rebuke in Quran 61:2?
A) Rebuking believers for past sins
B) Rebuking hypocrites for lying
C) Preventing a sin that has not yet been committed
D) Encouraging believers to speak truthfully

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that Quranic rebuke can be preventive, not just corrective.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quran 61:2, do you feel personally accused or do you see it as a protective warning from your Lord? Which response is more beneficial for your faith, and what will you do to cultivate the latter?
?
Think of a recent moment when you saw someone being tempted to do wrong. Did you offer a preventive word or remain silent? What holds you back from being a means of protection for others, and how can you change that starting today?

Iman Without Khushu': The Quranic Proof
Maturidi expounds on Quran 57:16 and draws two implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quran 57:16 to argue that iman remains valid even when a believer lacks khushu' (humility).

Core Idea
The Quran calls hard-hearted believers still 'believers'.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi analyzes a verse that rebukes believers for not having humble hearts, yet still calls them believers. He extracts two key points from this verse: first, that the name of iman is affirmed without khushu', and second, that God's rebuke is a reminder, not a denial of faith. This lesson focuses on the verse itself and its immediate implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic verse once and its literal translation. Notice that the verse addresses 'those who have believed' and then criticizes them.
2
Identify the two aspects
Maturidi explicitly says 'first' and 'second' after the verse. Find these two points.
The first is affirmation of iman without khushu'; the second is about God's rhetorical question.
3
Understand the implication
Reflect: if the verse still calls them believers, then khushu' cannot be a condition of iman. The rebuke is a admonishment, not a nullification.
This is the core argument against those who make khushu' essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال في قوله تعالى: ألم يأن للذين آمنوا أن تخشع قلوبهم لذكر الله وما نزل من الحق ولا يكونوا كالذين أوتوا الكتاب من قبل فطال عليهم الأمد فقست قلوبهم وكثير منهم فاسقون أنه أثبت اسم الإيمان وإن لم تخشع قلوبهم : إن أوّل ذلك إثبات اسم الإيمان بلا خشوع، وأنتم لا ترون إلا التصديق باللسان والمعرفة بالقلب. والثاني أن قد يقول لمن يخشى الله ويقوم بالغاية في شكره : أما ينبغي لك أن تخشاني وتشكرني ، لا أنه غير شاكر له، ولكن على التنبيه . قال الفقيه رحمه الله : فأما الأول فإنما الآية إنما هو في الخشوع لذكر الله، وأن من لا يخشع له مذموم فاسق وخشوع الإيمان هو الذي يكون بمعرفة جلاله وكبريائه، وهذا لا يزول عن المؤمن. ومع طول الأمد قد سُمّي مؤمنًا وإن كان به مذموما؛ وفي الآية دلالة طول ذلك فيهم، وذلك يوجب الوصف بالكبيرة عندهم ، وقد أبقى لهم اسم الإيمان، فبطل بذلك قولهم. والله الموفق. والثاني هو وصف من لا يعرف المنة والشكر فيعرض عن قبولها ويعاتب على ما كان حقه التعظيم والقبول . فإن كان هذا وصف الله عند المعتزلة فهو قد بلغ مناه من التسمي بأقبح اسم والخلود في أسفل الدرك. نعوذ بالله من الشقاء. ثم أطنب في هذا القول، لكن من أصل بنائه ما ذكرت فما يزيد إطنابه إلا بعدا عن الإصابة. وبالله المعونة.
Then He said regarding His statement, the Exalted: 'Has not the time come for those who have believed that their hearts should be humbly submissive (takhshaca) to the remembrance of Allah and what has come down of the truth, and that they should not be like those who were given the Scripture before, and the period became long for them, so their hearts became hardened, and many of them are defiantly disobedient?' — that He affirmed the name of iman even if their hearts are not humble. Indeed, first is the affirmation of the name of iman without khushu', and you do not see except affirmation with the tongue and knowledge with the heart. The second is that He may say to one who fears Allah and fulfills the utmost in His gratitude: 'Should you not fear Me and thank Me?' — not that he is ungrateful to Him, but as a reminder. The jurist (al-Faqih), may Allah have mercy on him, said: As for the first, the verse is about khushu' to the remembrance of Allah, and one who does not have it is blameworthy and a sinner. The khushu' of iman is that which comes from knowledge of His majesty and greatness, and this does not depart from the believer. And despite length of time, he is called a believer even if he is blameworthy for it. In the verse is an indication of that length in them, and that necessitates the description of major sin according to them, yet He retained for them the name of iman, so their saying is invalidated. And Allah is the Grantor of success. The second is a description of one who does not recognize the favor and gratitude, so he turns away from accepting it and rebukes what deserved glorification and acceptance. If this is the description of Allah according to the Mu'tazila, then he has attained his utmost in being named with the ugliest name and eternity in the lowest depth. We seek refuge with Allah from misery. Then he expounded on this statement, but from the foundation of his construction what I mentioned, so his elaboration only increases distance from correctness. And with Allah is help.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is both a Quranic interpretation and a refutation of the Mu'tazila. Maturidi examines Quran 57:16. The verse rebukes believers for not having humble hearts, but it still calls them 'believers'. Maturidi uses this to argue that iman does not require khushu' (humility) as a condition. He points to two aspects: first, the verse affirms iman without khushu'; second, God's rebuke is like a reminder to be grateful, not a denial of faith. The jurist's commentary reinforces that khushu' is a perfection, and its absence makes one blameworthy but not a disbeliever. The Mu'tazila claim khushu' is essential, but Maturidi says the verse preserves the name 'believer' for them, thus refuting their position. The second point is a harsh critique: if Mu'tazila attribute to God a rebuke that implies ingratitude, they have slandered God. Maturidi dismisses their elaboration as further error.

Key Terms
الخشوع
ذكر الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does Quran 57:16 affirm about those who lack khushu'?
A) They are not believers
B) They are still called believers
C) They become hypocrites
D) Their iman is invalid

Key Takeaway
The Quran affirms the name of iman even for believers whose hearts lack khushu'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship without any feeling of khushu', do you still consider yourself a true believer? How does this verse challenge the guilt that might make you doubt your iman?
?
God's rebuke to the grateful servant is described as a reminder, not an accusation. In your own life, where have you interpreted Allah's gentle reminders as harsh judgments? Will you now receive them as loving guidance?
?
This lesson separates iman from khushu', but are you comfortable with a faith that lacks humility? What concrete step will you take this week to cultivate khushu' not to 'earn' salvation but because you are already a believer?

The Nature of Khushu' in Iman: A Jurist's Commentary
The jurist explains the verse and refutes a heretical view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the khushu' that is a perfection of iman and the khushu' that is a condition, as explained by the jurist.

Core Idea
Khushu' is a perfection, not a condition, of iman.

After citing the verse, Maturidi presents the commentary of 'al-Faqih' (likely a previous scholar). This commentary clarifies that the khushu' mentioned in the verse is a specific kind — khushu' to the remembrance of Allah — which comes from knowledge of His majesty. This kind of khushu' never leaves a true believer, even if they are blameworthy. The jurist uses this to refute those who claim that absence of khushu' removes iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the jurist's commentary
Read the Arabic passage starting with 'قال الفقيه' and its translation. Note that the jurist distinguishes between two types of khushu'.
2
Identify the two types
The jurist mentions khushu' to remembrance (which can be lacking) and khushu' of iman (from knowledge of Allah). The latter never leaves the believer.
This distinction is crucial to refute the Mu'tazila.
3
Understand the refutation
The jurist says the verse preserves the name 'believer', so the Mu'tazili claim that lack of khushu' negates iman is invalidated.
The verse indication of 'length' suggests they are major sinners, not disbelievers.

Refuting the Mu'tazili Position on Khushu'
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazili interpretation and warns against misattributing to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's harsh refutation of the Mu'tazila who claim that lack of khushu' implies ingratitude or disbelief.

Core Idea
Attributing ingratitude to God through misinterpretation is a grave error.

Maturidi concludes his argument by addressing the second point from the verse: God's rhetorical question to the grateful servant. He turns this into a sharp critique of the Mu'tazila. If they interpret God's words as implying that the servant is ungrateful, they are attributing to God an 'ugly name' and deserving eternal punishment. Maturidi dismisses their elaborate reasoning as only increasing distance from truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'والثاني' to the end. Understand that Maturidi describes someone who does not recognize favor and is rebuked.
2
Apply to Mu'tazila
Maturidi says if this is what the Mu'tazila attribute to Allah, then they have described Allah with the ugliest name.
This is a very serious charge.
3
Recognize the dismissal
Maturidi states that their elaboration only increases error. The foundation of his argument refutes them sufficiently.

?
If someone accused you of being ungrateful when you were trying your best, how would you feel? Now consider: when you read verses of warning or rebuke, do you project that same false accusation onto God? Repent and resolve to see His guidance as pure kindness.

Fighting Does Not Expel from Iman
Maturidi explains Quran 49:9-10, arguing that fighting does not remove one from iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quran 49:9-10 to argue that fighting between believers does not negate their iman, and how he refutes the view that major sin removes one from faith.

Core Idea
The Quran calls them believers even as they fight — iman remains.

In this passage, Maturidi tackles a challenging verse that might seem to suggest fighting removes one from faith. He carefully unpacks the Quranic wording to show that the fighters are still called 'believers', and that their sins — even major ones — do not erase iman. Through comparisons and logical refutations, he establishes a key Maturidi principle: major sin does not negate iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow of argument: Maturidi begins with a direct answer, then considers possible counter-arguments, and ends with a refutation of an opposing view.
2
Identify Maturidi's initial argument
Maturidi compares the verse to the apostasy verse (2:217) where a person is called a believer before reverting. Similarly, the fighters are called 'believers' before the fighting, showing that fighting does not remove iman.
He also mentions two possible explanations for the fighting: without weapons or as mujtahids.
3
Understand his refutation of those explanations
Maturidi argues that if the fighters were mujtahids, the command to reform would not make sense. The command to fight the transgressor shows the transgressor was known, not a mujtahid. Also, the presence of the Prophet precludes ijtihad.
4
Follow his conclusion and refutation of Al-Ka'bi
Maturidi concludes that the command to fight indicates the sin is major, yet God retains the name 'believer'. Then he refutes Al-Ka'bi's claim that a major sinner should not be prayed for, since reform (islah) includes prayer for good.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أجاب في قوله : وإن طائفتان من المؤمنين اقتتلوا الآية، أنه كقوله : ومن يرتدد منكم عن دينه وقد كان سماه مؤمنا من قبل والثاني أن يكون الاقتتال بغير سلاح نحو المجاذبة، أو كانوا مجتهدين فلا يخرجون به من الإيمان. فيقال: إذ جرى الأمر بالإصلاح بينهم وتسمية الإخوة بطل معنى الردّة. وقوله : فقاتلوا التي تبغى دل أن الباغي كان معلوماً، لا أن كان ثمة اجتهاد. مع ما كان رسول الله الله بين أظهرهم أنّى لهم الاجتهاد إلى ذلك الحد? ثم دل الأمر بالقتال ـ والصغيرة تكون مغفورة لا يقابل عليها - على أن ذنوبهم قد كبرت، وقد أبقى الله لهم اسم الإيمان. والله الموفق. وقال في قوله : إنما المؤمنون إخوة بمثل ذلك، وقد بينا وهمه . ثم على قوله إن صاحب الكبيرة عدو الله لا يسع له الدعاء بالخير ويلزم لعنه، وما الإصلاح إلا الدعاء بالخير والصلاح ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then he answered regarding His statement: 'And if two groups of the believers fight, then make peace between them' — that it is like His statement: 'And whoever of you reverts from his religion...' while He had called him a believer before. And the second is that the fighting is without weapons, like grappling, or they were mujtahids, so they do not exit from iman thereby. It is said: When the matter of reform between them and the naming of brothers occurs, the meaning of apostasy is nullified. And His statement: 'Fight the one that transgresses' indicates that the transgressor was known, not that there was ijtihad. Especially when the Messenger of Allah was among them, how could they have ijtihad to that extent? Then the command to fight — and a small sin is forgiven and not retaliated for — indicates that their sins were great, yet Allah retained for them the name of iman. And Allah is the Grantor of success. And he said regarding His statement: 'The believers are but brothers' similarly, and we have shown his error. Then upon his statement that the perpetrator of a major sin is an enemy of Allah, it is not permissible to pray for good for him, and cursing him is obligatory, while reform is nothing but prayer for good and righteousness. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Al-Ka'bi regarding Quran 49:9-10. Maturidi first notes that the verse calls the fighting parties 'believers', just as the verse on apostasy (2:217) calls a person a believer before apostasy. This shows fighting does not remove one from iman. He considers two explanations: either the fighting is non-lethal, or the fighters were mujtahids (mistaken but excused). But then he counters: the verse commands reform and calls them brothers, which negates the idea of apostasy. The command to fight the transgressor shows the transgressor was known, not a mujtahid. Moreover, the Prophet being present precludes ijtihad. The fact that fighting is commanded and small sins are forgiven indicates that the sins here are major, yet God retains the name 'believer'. Finally, Maturidi refutes Al-Ka'bi's claim that the major sinner is an enemy of God not to be prayed for, arguing that reform (islah) necessarily includes prayer for good.

Key Terms
طائفتان من المؤمنين
الاقتتال
الاجتهاد
الباغي
الإصلاح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think fighting believers makes them disbelievers.
Correction: Maturidi proves the Quran still calls them believers, so fighting does not negate iman.

Checkpoint
How does Maturidi use Quran 49:9 to argue that major sin does not negate iman?
A) The verse calls the fighters 'believers'
B) The verse commands them to repent
C) The verse says they are enemies of God
D) The verse allows killing them

Key Takeaway
Fighting between believers, even if sinful, does not remove them from the fold of iman.

?

This passage shows that even fighting—a grave sin—does not remove the name of iman. Are you using that as an excuse to neglect repentance, or does it drive you to thank Allah for His mercy and strive to change? Be honest: are you complacent?
?
