Muhkam and Mutashābih in Maturidi's Thought
Maturidi divides revelation into muhkam/mutashābih and mufassar/mubham, explaining their purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's division of revelation into clear (muhkam) and ambiguous (mutashābih) verses, the purpose of this division, and how it functions as a test for believers.

Core Idea
Revelation's ambiguity is not a flaw but a divine test of submission and inquiry.

In this passage from his Kitab al-Tawhid, Imam Maturidi explains that Allah divided revelation into clear and ambiguous sections to define the boundaries of knowledge and to test His servants. He outlines a method for interpreting ambiguous verses by the clear ones, and warns against sectarian misuse. This foundational discussion sets the stage for understanding how early Muslim scholars approached theological differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Notice that Maturidi mentions two pairs: muhkam/mutashabih and mufassar/mubham. Understand that these are two ways of classifying revelation.
The terms mufassar and mubham are sometimes used interchangeably with muhkam and mutashabih.
2
Understand the purpose
The division serves to clarify limits: when to refrain and when to proceed. It also functions as a test through submission (taslim) and inquiry (talab).
Maturidi emphasizes that the servant's duty is obedience according to the capacity of the command.
3
Learn the method of interpretation
The correct method is to interpret the obscure (mubham) in light of the explicable (mufassar). The ambiguous (mutashabih) should be examined against the clear (muhkam) to see if it aligns.
If understanding is not necessary, one may refrain from delving — that restraint itself becomes a test.
4
Reflect on the historical outcome
Maturidi notes that each sect thought it had grasped the muhkam, leading to divergence. This creates the need to know how to distinguish.
He concludes that the Quran is free from contradiction, citing verse 4:82.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم جعل السمع قسمين : محكم ومتشابه ومفسر ومبهم ، ليبين منتهى المعارف من الكف فيما يجب ذلك والإقدام فيما يلزمه ، ومن حمل المبهم على المفسر ، لزم المحكم وعرض المتشابه عليه ما أمكن أن يكون ما فيه مما يلزم تعرفه ومما إليه حاجة بأهل المحنة ، أو ترك الخوض فى ذلك فيما أمكن الغنا عن تعرف حقيقة ما فيه ، فيكون محنة الوقوف ؛ إذ الله تعالى يمتحن بوجهين : بالتسليم مرة وبالطلب ثانيا ، وإنما على العبد الطاعة فى قدر الأمر ، ولما جمع جل ثناؤه كتابه على الأمرين يعرف الناس الدين، أقروا بالكتاب أنه حق من عند الله لا العدول عنه ، وأن من لزمه أفلح ونجا ، ومن مال عنه شقى وخسر ، حتى ظن كل فريق أنه قد أصاب المحكم من ذلك ولزمه ، وأن عليه فيما ذهب إليه خصومه أن يقف في ذلك أو يجمله على ما تقرر عنده فيما اعتقده ، فألزم تفرقهم الحاجة ، كلا يعرف المحكم من المتشابه لزوم العلم بالمتشابه أن لا يتناقض المحكم ثم معلوم أنه لا يحتمل القرآن الاختلاف ، و به وصف الله أنه وَلَوْ كَانَ
Then He made revelation two divisions: muhkam (clear) and mutashābih (ambiguous), mufassar (explicable) and mubham (obscure), to clarify the limits of knowledge regarding refraining where that is necessary and proceeding where it is required. And whoever carries the obscure upon the explicable, he adheres to the muhkam and presents the mutashābih to it as much as possible, so that what is in it may be either what is necessary to know and what the people of trial need, or to refrain from delving into that when one can do without knowing its reality, so that it becomes a trial of stopping; for Allah tests in two ways: by submission once and by inquiry a second time. And the servant's duty is only obedience according to the extent of the command. And when Allah, exalted is His mention, compiled His Book upon the two matters so that people may know the religion, they affirmed that the Book is truth from Allah, no deviation from it, and that whoever adheres to it succeeds and is saved, and whoever turns away from it is wretched and lost. Until each faction thought that it had attained the muhkam from it and adhered to it, and that it is upon its opponents to stop in that or to summarize it according to what is established with them in their belief. So their divergence necessitated the need for each to know the muhkam from the mutashābih out of necessity, that the muhkam does not contradict. Then it is known that the Quran does not admit contradiction, and by it Allah described it as 'And if it had been' [from other than Allah, they would have found much contradiction].
Source pages p. 821

Commentary
This passage explains the divisions within revelation (al-samʿ). Maturidi states that God made revelation two divisions: muhkam (clear) and mutashābih (ambiguous), and also mufassar (explicable) and mubham (obscure). The purpose is to clarify the limits of knowledge: when to refrain and when to proceed. The proper method is to interpret the obscure in light of the explicable, adhering to the muhkam. If the meaning is not necessary, one may refrain from delving into it, and that becomes a test of standing still. God tests people in two ways: by submission (taslīm) and by inquiry (ṭalab). The servant's duty is obedience to the extent of command. Then Maturidi notes that since the Quran contains these two aspects, people accepted it as truth. But each sect thought it had grasped the muhkam and insisted that opponents should stop or follow their interpretation. This divergence created the need to distinguish muhkam from mutashābih, and it is known that the Quran does not contain contradiction, as God says in the verse (4:82) implying that if it were from other than God, there would be much contradiction.

Key Terms

المتشابه
المفسر
المبهم
التسليم
الطلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Quranic verses are equally clear and any ambiguity is a flaw.
Correction: Maturidi shows that ambiguity is intentional as a test for believers through submission and inquiry.

Checkpoint
What are the two ways God tests people according to this passage?
A) Through wealth and poverty
B) Through submission (taslīm) and inquiry (ṭalab)
C) Through life and death
D) Through reward and punishment

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's division of revelation into clear and ambiguous serves both to guide believers and to test their faith, with the Quran remaining free from contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Maturidi says each faction thought it had attained the muhkam. Where in your own life—perhaps in a theological opinion or a personal conviction—have you assumed your understanding is the only clear one? Can you name one area where you might be wrong?
?
The passage says the Quran does not admit contradiction. If you have ever felt two verses contradict, how does this teaching challenge you to reconcile them instead of dismissing one? What personal effort will you make to resolve that tension?

Forgiveness Across All Sins: Quranic Refutation of Mu'tazila and Khawarij
Maturidi uses Quranic verses on recompense to refute Mu'tazila and Khawarij positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi uses specific Quranic verses to argue that forgiveness can cover both major and minor sins, contradicting the strict views of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Forgiveness is possible for all sins, refuting absolute denial by sects.

Imam al-Maturidi now engages in a polemical argument, citing Quranic verses that promise recompense for good and evil, and verses that explicitly promise forgiveness and transformation of evil deeds. He uses these to counter the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, who held that major sins cannot be forgiven without repentance. Read the passage to see how the verses themselves reveal a broader mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the sequence of Quranic citations and Maturidi's comments.
The passage is dense; take your time with each phrase.
2
Identify the Quranic verses cited
List the three or four verses Maturidi quotes. Look for the markers: 'قال' and 'وقوله'.
The verses are: 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good...', 'Whoever does evil or wrongs himself...', 'If they desist, what has passed will be forgiven...', 'God will replace their evil deeds with good ones.'
3
Understand Maturidi's deduction from each verse
For each verse, ask: What point does Maturidi derive? The first verse shows recompense for good; the second shows recompense for evil; the third and fourth show that forgiveness and transformation are possible.
Pay attention to how he connects the verses to the possibility of forgiveness for both major and minor sins.
4
See how this refutes the target sects
Maturidi explicitly states that this conclusion does not hold for the Mu'tazila (for major or minor sins) nor for the Khawarij. Why? Because they denied forgiveness for major sins unless repentance occurred. The verses suggest otherwise.
The phrase 'وذلك لا يكون على قول المعتزلة... وكذا فى قول الخوارج' directly connects the argument to the refutation.
5
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider what this teaches about divine mercy and the need for repentance. Maturidi is not claiming automatic forgiveness without conditions, but he is affirming that forgiveness is not restricted only to minor sins.
This guards against the extreme view that God cannot forgive grave sins except with strict conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا إن الله تعالى قال : فَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ ، ثم معلوم أنه لا يرى الخير ، وجزاه مع الشرك ، ولا جزاه شر في حال الكفر يرى ذلك بعد الإيمان لقوله تعالى : وَمَنْ يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا أَوْ يَظْلِمْ نَفْسَهُ ، وقوله : 'وَإِنْ يَنْتَهُوا يُغْفَرْ لَهُمْ مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ' ، وقال : 'فَأُولَئِكَ يُبَدِّلُ اللهُ سَيِّئَاتِهِم حَسَنَاتٍ'، دل ما ذكرت من تحقيق حال فيها جزاء الأمرين، وذلك لا يكون على قول المعتزلة فى وقت الكبائر ولا فى وقت الصغائر ، وكذا فى قول الخوارج ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also God Almighty said: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it.' Then it is known that he does not see the good, and his recompense with shirk, and he is not recompensed evil in the state of disbelief, he sees that after faith due to His saying: 'And whoever does evil or wrongs himself,' and His saying: 'And if they desist, what has passed will be forgiven them,' and He said: 'Those are the ones for whom God will replace their evil deeds with good ones.' So what I have mentioned indicates the reality of the matter concerning the recompense of both matters, and that is not according to the saying of the Mu'tazila at the time of the major sins nor at the time of the minor sins, and likewise according to the saying of the Khawarij. And there is no power except with God.

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from Quranic verses that contradict the Mu'tazila and Khawarij views. Maturidi cites verses that promise seeing the recompense of good and evil, and verses indicating forgiveness for those who desist and replacement of evil with good. He argues that these verses show that forgiveness is possible for both major and minor sins contrary to the strict positions of the two sects.

Misconception: The Quranic verses about recompense prove that all sins are automatically forgiven without any condition.
Correction: Maturidi does not claim automatic forgiveness; he argues that forgiveness is possible for both major and minor sins, but the context implies that repentance (as in 'if they desist') is a condition. His aim is to refute the absolute denial of forgiveness, not to assert unconditional pardon.

Hypocrisy and Its Signs in Major Sins
Maturidi defines hypocrisy and supports with Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi links hypocrisy (nifāq) to major sins using Quranic verses and a hadith about three telltale signs.

Core Idea
Hypocrisy is revealed when actions contradict faith—and major sins expose this.

Maturidi now turns from polytheism and disbelief to hypocrisy. He argues that hypocrisy is not a separate category but is evidenced by actions that contradict one's verbal faith. He supports this with Quranic tests and a prophetic hadith outlining three telltale signs. This passage shows how major sins can be outward indicators of inner hypocrisy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to understand the flow of Maturidi's argument.
Notice the shift from earlier discussions on shirk and kufr.
2
Identify Maturidi's definition of hypocrisy
Look for the phrase 'contradicting what he gave with his tongue of faith'. This is the core definition.
Hypocrisy here is practical inconsistency, not just disbelief.
3
Examine the Quranic verses
Two verses are cited: one stating God will distinguish believers from hypocrites, another indicating testing to reveal truthfulness. Consider how they support the argument.
Both are from Surah al-‘Ankabut.
4
Analyze the hadith on three signs
The hadith lists three characteristics: lying, breaking promises, betraying trusts. Understand each and why they are signs of hypocrisy.
This hadith is well-known and often cited.
5
Grasp the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that these signs are 'apparent from the committers of major sins'. This links hypocrisy directly to sinful behavior.
He does not say every major sinner is a hypocrite, but that the signs are found in them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدخل تسمية الشرك والكفر فيما مر بيانه ، ومن حقق له اسم النفاق فمخالفة ما أعطى بلسانه من الايمان وتعاهد حدوده وحفظ حدود الله ما ظهر بأفعالهم ، و بذلك قال الله تعالى : وَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَلَيَعْلَمَنَّ المُنَافِقِينَ ، وقال : الم ، أَحَسِبَ النَّاسُ أَنْ يُتْرَكُوا ، أخبر ببيان ما أعطته الألسن من الصدق والكذب بالمحنة . وكذا روى عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : ثلاث من كن فيه فهو منافق : من إذا حدث كذب ، وإذا وعد خلف ، وإذا اوتمن خان . فقد ظهر له ذلك كله من مرتكبى الكبيرة ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
So the naming of polytheism (shirk) and disbelief entered into what has been explained. And the one for whom the name of hypocrisy (nifāq) is verified—it is because of contradicting what he gave with his tongue of faith, and his [breach of] covenants of its limits and preserving God's limits that appeared in their actions. And with that God, exalted, said: 'And God will surely know those who believe and will surely know the hypocrites.' And He said: 'Alif Lām Mīm. Do people think that they will be left [untested]?' He informed of the clarification of what the tongues give of truth and falsehood through trial. And likewise it was narrated from the Messenger of God (God bless him and grant peace) that he said: 'Three [characteristics]—whoever has them in him is a hypocrite: one who when he speaks he lies, when he promises he breaks, and when he is entrusted he betrays.' So all of that has become apparent from the committers of major sins. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 930

Commentary
This passage is an argument linking hypocrisy (nifāq) to major sins. Maturidi states that the naming of polytheism and disbelief is already covered, and now he turns to hypocrisy: one is rightly called a hypocrite if his actions contradict his verbal confession of faith and the limits set by God. He supports this with two Quranic verses. The first, from Surah al-‘Ankabut, says that God will distinguish the believers from the hypocrites through testing. The second (also from al-‘Ankabut) indicates that people are tested to reveal the truthfulness or falsehood of their tongues. Then he cites a well-known hadith: three traits—lying, breaking promises, betraying trusts—are signs of hypocrisy. Maturidi concludes that these traits are clearly found in those who commit major sins, implying that such sinners manifest hypocrisy and thus their claim to true faith is compromised. He ends with 'There is no power except with God.'

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith about the three signs of hypocrisy refers to absolute disbelief (kufr) and that anyone displaying them is a complete hypocrite outside Islam.
Correction: Maturidi uses the hadith to show that these signs are present in major sinners, not that they are necessarily full hypocrites. The signs indicate a shortfall in faith, not outright apostasy.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the prophetic signs of hypocrisy are observable in major sinners, linking sinful behavior to a deficiency in faith.

Consensus on Intercession and Prayer for Dead Believers
Maturidi cites consensus and community practice to affirm intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus and continuous practice of the Muslim community confirm intercession for all believers, including those who committed major sins.

Core Idea
The community's practice proves intercession for all who die facing the qibla.

Maturidi appeals to two strong proofs: the consensus of transmitters on intercession and the unbroken practice of the community praying over every Muslim who dies, seeking forgiveness and mercy. This shows that even believers with major sins remain part of the community and are eligible for intercession. This passage defends the authenticity of hadith on intercession and the authority of the guiding imams.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the two distinct arguments Maturidi presents.
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the two arguments
Identify the consensus of transmitters on intercession and the community's practice of praying for all who die facing the qibla.
3
Reflect on why community practice is a proof
Consider how the continuous practice (tawārutḥ) of the ummah serves as evidence that intercession is for all believers, even sinners.
This practice has been passed down since the Prophet's time.
4
Connect to hadith and imams
Maturidi states this proof is for those who refuse to belie authentic hadith and oppose guiding imams. Understand the role of tradition in this argument.
5
Consider the implication for sinners
The passage implies that believers who commit major sins are still entitled to intercession and prayer, contrary to some views.
This is a key point in Islamic theology about the fate of sinful believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إجماع النقلة في إثبات الشفاعة. وتوارث الأمة في الصلاة على جميع من مات القبلة والاستغفار لهم والترحم عليهم هو الدليل لمن أبت نفسه تكذيب الأخبار الصحاح ومخالفة أئمة الهدى، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the consensus of the transmitters on affirming intercession. And the successive practice of the community in praying over all who die facing the qibla, and seeking forgiveness for them, and having mercy on them, is the proof for one whose soul refuses to belie the authentic reports and to oppose the guiding imams. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 933

Commentary
This passage presents a consensus-based argument. Maturidi states that there is consensus (ijmāʿ) among the transmitters (naqalah) of the community on affirming intercession (shafāʿah) for believers. Additionally, the continuous practice (tawārutḥ) of the Muslim community (al-ummah) is to pray the funeral prayer over all those who die facing the qibla (i.e., Muslims), to seek forgiveness (istighfār) for them, and to have mercy (tarahḥum) on them. This practice includes believers who committed major sins. This serves as a clear proof for anyone who refuses to deny the authentic ḥadīth (akhbār ṣiḥāḥ) and to oppose the guiding imams. The implication is that this consensus and practice confirm that those who die with faith, even if sinners, remain believers and are entitled to intercession and prayer.

Key Terms
إجماع
شفاعة
استغفار
ترحم
قبلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only sinless believers are prayed for and eligible for intercession.
Correction: The community's practice of praying for all who die facing the qibla shows that even believers with major sins are considered part of the ummah and are eligible for intercession.

Checkpoint

B) That intercession is only for prophets.
C) That those who die facing the qibla are believers regardless of sins.
D) That funeral prayer is optional for sinners.

Key Takeaway
The consensus and continuous practice of the community affirm that intercession covers all believers, including those who committed major sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you have ever felt that a fellow believer's sins were too great for Allah's mercy, what does this passage say about your own understanding of God's mercy? Will you commit to praying for every deceased Muslim without exception, trusting in the intercession affirmed by consensus?

The Third Point: Equality of Punishment for Major Sins
Maturidi argues that eternal punishment is the equivalent of the polytheist's evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that eternal punishment for the polytheist is the exact equivalent (mithl) of his evil, based on the verse 'Whoever comes with an evil deed will not be repaid except its like.'

Core Idea
Eternal punishment is the just equivalent of persistent polytheism.

Maturidi tackles a difficult question: how can the eternal punishment of the polytheist be just when the Qur'an says evil deeds are repaid only with their like? This passage presents a sophisticated argument that eternal consignment is in fact the precise equivalent of the polytheist's own evil, because the disbeliever would choose it over deliverance. The argument reveals the depth of Maturidi's commitment to divine justice and the rational coherence of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
The verse 'Whoever comes with an evil deed will not be repaid except its like' seems to imply a proportional punishment, which might exclude eternal punishment for polytheists. Recognize why this is a challenge.
2
Maturidi's claim
Maturidi asserts that eternal punishment is the 'like' (mithl) of the polytheist's evil. Identify where this claim is made in the passage.
The phrase 'فثبت أن مثل سيئته هو الخلود في العذاب' establishes this.
3
The key argument
The stubborn disbeliever, if offered the choice, would accept eternal punishment over deliverance. This shows that eternal punishment is the precise equivalent of his evil. Trace how Maturidi uses this reasoning.
4
Two corollaries
Maturidi draws two implications: (1) if eternal punishment were not the like, it would imply lying about God's promise; (2) punishing a lesser sinner with the same would be unjust. Notice how these reinforce the argument.
The passage mentions 'فيدخل فيه أمران'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث أنه لم يبين في الكبائر قدر العقوبات، ومثل الشرك والمعاندة إنما هو معلوم أن الله نفى أن يجزى أن ليس التخليد، ولا ريب لى السيئات إلا مثلها، بعاند ولا مشرك له فى العبادة ذنبه دون من يفعل ذلك، بل صحة الاعتقاد في ذلك حمله على الخوف مما حذره ورجاء ما أطمعه فى الاعتقاد، وهو الذي سبق لم يجز أن يكون قدر ذنبه قدر الأول، فلم يجز كل شيء لكفره هو ومحاه عنه، أن يخلد فى ذلك، فيدخل فيه أمران: أحدهما الكذب في الوعد حيث قال: وَمَنْ جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَلَا يُجْزَى إِلَّا مِثْلَهَا، ومعلوم أن الكافر المعاند لو جمع ما يعاقب به على شرط النجاة والراحة يحتمل ويختاره، فثبت أن مثل سيئته هو الخلود في العذاب، فإذا عُذب يمثله من كان ذنبه دونه كان جازيا أكثر ما يُعاقب بما يرتكب "، وفى الحكمة عقوبته، وهذا مما يمنع من مثله، وهو الحكمه، والله الموفق .
And the third [point] is that He did not specify the measure of punishments for major sins. And the example of polytheism and stubbornness is that it is known that God negated that He rewards except the like of evil deeds, and there is no doubt that [eternal] consignment is not [the like]? For the stubborn and polytheist in worship his sin is not less than one who does that? Rather, soundness of belief in that leads him to fear what He warned and hope for what He promised in belief. And that which preceded is not such that his sin's measure equals the former's? Thus it is not permissible that all things for his disbelief and its erasure, that he be consigned eternally in that? So it includes two matters: one is lying about the promise where He said: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed will not be repaid except its like' (6:160). And it is known that the stubborn disbeliever, if he were to gather that with which he is punished on condition of deliverance and rest, he would accept and choose it. So it is established that the like of his evil deed is eternal consignment in punishment. So if one whose sin is less than his is punished with its like, then He would be rewarding more than what he commits? And in wisdom his punishment, and this prevents its like? And it is the wisdom, and Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 938

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the justice of eternal punishment for polytheists. Maturidi begins by stating the third point: God did not specify the exact measure of punishment for major sins. The example of polytheism and stubbornness shows that it is known that God negates rewarding except the like of evil deeds. There is doubt about eternal consignment not being the like? — but the argument seeks to prove that eternal punishment is indeed the equivalent (mithl). Maturidi argues that the stubborn polytheist's sin is not less than that of another, and sound belief leads to fear and hope. The preceding statement shows that his sin's measure cannot equal that of the first (the less sinful). Therefore, his disbelief erases his good deeds, so it is permissible to consign him eternally. Two consequences follow: first, it would be lying about the promise if eternal punishment is not the like, but the verse 'Whoever comes with an evil deed will not be repaid except its like' (6:160) applies. The stubborn disbeliever, if offered the option, would accept eternal punishment over deliverance, so his evil's like is eternal punishment. If one with a lesser sin is punished with the same like, then God would be punishing more than what the lesser one deserves? But the wisdom in His punishment prevents this. Thus, the argument establishes that eternal punishment for the polytheist is the exact equivalent of his evil, consistent with divine justice.

Key Terms
الكبائر
الشرك
المعاندة
التخليد
المثل
الوعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Whoever comes with an evil deed will not be repaid except its like' implies that no punishment can be eternal, because evil deeds are finite.
Correction: Maturidi argues that eternal punishment is indeed the 'like' of the polytheist's evil because the polytheist's evil is so great that its equivalent is eternal; the disbeliever would choose eternal punishment over deliverance, confirming it as the like.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the 'like' (mithl) of the polytheist's evil deed?
A) Temporary punishment
B) Eternal consignment in punishment
C) Forgiveness
D) Reward equal to good deeds

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that the Quranic principle of just recompense is consistent with eternal punishment for polytheism, because the polytheist's evil is so great that only eternal punishment is its equal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to stand before God and He asked why you ignored His warnings about sin, what would your answer be? The polytheist in the lesson would accept eternal punishment rather than give up his disbelief. Is there any sin in your life you hold onto so tightly that you would rather face its consequences than abandon it? Today, identify that sin and resolve to repent from it, knowing God's justice is perfect.
?
This lesson shows that God's promise of 'like for like' is true and just. Look at your own actions over the past week. What 'like' have you stored up? Are you comfortable with what you deserve? If not, what will you change today to seek God's mercy before it's too late? Pray for a heart that fears His justice and hopes in His mercy.
?
The polytheist would choose eternal punishment over deliverance because his evil had consumed him. Have you become so accustomed to a particular sin that you no longer feel its weight? Let this lesson shake you: God's punishment is precisely what fits the crime. Do not wait until you are face to face with the fire to repent. Commit now to one concrete step away from that sin.

Three Answers to the Objection on the Promise
Maturidi gives three answers to an objection that the promise is false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi defends the consistency of God's promise by offering three nuanced interpretative answers to an objection.

Core Idea
God's promise is not false; it must be interpreted contextually.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses an objection that a particular verse undermines the divine promise, making it seem false. He presents three distinct answers that show how the promise remains true when understood properly. These answers demonstrate the depth of kalam reasoning in defending core beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the objection
Notice how the opponents claim the promise is false. The author describes their stance and the verse they use.
The verse mentioned is 'Gardens' based on what they said.
2
First answer: reference to final states
The verse is informing about the ultimate outcome, which every believer refers to. This answer contextualizes the verse as describing the final result, not an immediate promise.
3
Second answer: promise for true believers
The promise applies specifically to those who have achieved faith with its true character. Naming someone based on associated matters is permissible.
This answer qualifies the recipients of the promise.
4
Third answer: reward and punishment according to rights
Reward and punishment are based on one's due rights. Suffering for one's religion does not mean falling short; God's bounty is great.
This answer emphasizes God's wisdom in distributing reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا بهم الوعد كذب، لا يزال يجعله مفزعا لنفسه في كل نائبة، وقد قال الله بما قالوا جنات، وليس يجب مثله للقول، خاصة في قول الجميع فثبت به كذبه في الحكاية. ثم لما استدل بالآيات أجوبة ثلاثة: أحدها الإخبار عن منتهى الأحوال، وإلى ذلك مرجع كل مؤمن. والثاني أن يكون الوعد للذين حققوا الإيمان بأخلاقه، وما دل عليه، وجائز تسمية أحد بشيء، ذلك اسم لأمر تتصل به أمور عند جميع تلك الأمور، ويجوز عند إقرار الاسم بالذي به سمي، والله أعلم. والثالث أن يكون له ذلك الجزاء، وما يعاقب به، فهو يعاقب بحقوقه، وليس الذي يصيبه بحق دينه مقصر عنه حق دينه. مع ما بين الله أن له فضلا كبيرا؛ ليعلم أن الجزاء للخيرات منه أفضال، وما كان من حكمة الأفضال فإلى من يقوم به ذلك من اختيار أحوال وأوقات.
And lo, they [deem] the promise false, he does not cease to make it a refuge for himself in every calamity, and Allah has said: 'Because of what they said, gardens,' and the like of it is not necessary for the statement, especially in the statement of all, so his falsehood in the narration is established. Then when he used the verses as evidence, [there are] three answers: one of them is informing about the final states, and to that is the reference of every believer. And the second is that the promise is for those who realized faith with its character, and what it indicates, and it is permissible to name someone with a thing, that is a name for a matter to which matters are connected in all those matters, and it is permissible upon affirming the name by what he is named, and Allah knows best. And the third is that he will have that reward, and what he is punished with, so he is punished according to his rights, and what befalls him due to his religion is not falling short of his religion's right. Along with what Allah made clear that He has great bounty, so that it may be known that the reward for good deeds is from His bounties, and whatever [comes] from the wisdom of bounties, it is for the one who performs that from the choice of states and times.
Source pages p. 945

Commentary
This passage is a set of three answers (أجوبة ثلاثة) given by the author to an objection regarding the divine promise (الوعد). The objection claims that a particular verse undermines the promise, making it seem false. The author begins by describing the situation: the opponents consider the promise false and rely on the verse that says 'gardens' in response to what they said. The three answers follow:
1. The first answer interprets the verse as referring to the ultimate outcome (منتهى الأحوال) which all believers refer to.
2. The second answer specifies that the promise is for those who have realized faith with its true character and that naming is permissible based on the associated matters.
3. The third answer clarifies that the reward and punishment are based on one's rights, and that any suffering due to one's religion does not detract from the religion's right, emphasizing that God's bounty is great and rewards are from His favor.
This passage shows how the author defends the consistency of God's promise by providing nuanced interpretations.

Key Terms

الإخبار
الحكاية
الأجوبة الثلاثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The promise of God can be rendered false by a general statement in the Quran.
Correction: The passage shows that such statements must be interpreted contextually, and the promise remains true through these three answers.

Refutation from the Verse of Slander
Maturidi refutes an argument from the verse of slander.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the claim that the verse of slander proves a cursed person cannot be a believer.

Core Idea
A conditional curse does not make someone a non-believer.

This passage deals with a specific argument from the verse of slander (Quran 24:6-7). The opponent tries to use this verse to argue that a person who is cursed cannot be a believer. Maturidi responds by pointing out that the curse is conditional ("if he is of the liars") and that the verse does not actually name the person cursed. This shows how careful attention to Quranic wording is essential in theological argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opponent's argument
The opponent claims that since Allah says they are cursed without mentioning deeming it lawful, the cursed one is not a believer.
This is based on a reading of the verse that ignores its conditional nature.
2
Read the verse of slander
Refer to Quran 24:6-7 to see the actual wording: the curse is invoked "if he is of the liars."
The verse does not say Allah has cursed them unconditionally.
3
Notice Maturidi's first objection
Maturidi accuses the opponent of lying about the Quran by misrepresenting the verse.
This is a strong rhetorical move—highlighting distortion of scripture.
4
Grasp the second point: conditional curse
The curse is conditional upon being a liar; it does not automatically remove one from faith.
Maturidi emphasizes that the verse does not deny the person's belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج بآية القذف إن الله أخبر أنهم ملعونون بلا ذكر استحلال وغيره. ولا يكون الملعون مؤمنا بقول، وبالله التوفيق. إنما في الآية لعنة الله عليه إن كان كذلك، وليس فيها أن الله سماه ملعونا. فأول ما في اعتلائك أن كذبت على القرآن، ثم كيف ألزمته اللعنة بقوله: {أَنَّ لَعْنَةَ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ إِنْ كَانَ مِنَ الْكَاذِبِينَ} ولم يلزمه اسم الإيمان، وهو يقول به. ويحقق أيضا أنه رد أحد اللعنتين إلى الحد، و
Then he argued with the verse of slander: 'Indeed, Allah informed that they are cursed without mention of deeming lawful or otherwise.' And the cursed one is not a believer by statement, and with Allah is success. But in the verse is 'the curse of Allah be upon him if he is of the liars,' and there is not in it that Allah named him cursed. So the first thing in your argument is that you lied against the Quran, then how do you compel the curse upon him by His saying: 'That the curse of Allah be upon him if he is of the liars'? And he does not compel the name of faith upon him, and he is a believer by it. And he also asserts that he referred one of the two curses to the punishment, and
Source pages p. 946

Commentary
This passage refutes an argument based on the verse of slander (آية القذف, Quran 24:6-7). The opponent claims that the verse states that the accusers are cursed without requiring them to deem the act lawful, implying they are not believers. The author counters that the verse actually says 'that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is of the liars,' not that Allah himself names them cursed. The author accuses the opponent of lying about the Quran and points out that the verse does not deny faith. The argument is incomplete at the end.

Misconception: The verse of slander proves that the accuser is automatically a non-believer because Allah curses them.
Correction: The curse in the verse is conditional ('if he is of the liars'), not a direct declaration of unbelief. Maturidi shows that the verse does not name the person cursed; it invokes a curse conditionally.

Faith Remains Despite Failure to Emigrate or Accept Greeting
Maturidi proves that not emigrating does not negate faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that certain omitted actions like not emigrating or not responding to a greeting do not negate faith according to Maturidi's proof from the Quran.

Core Idea
Not emigrating does not remove faith; it only affects guardianship.

Maturidi addresses a critical question: does failing to perform certain actions nullify one's faith? He turns to two Quranic verses that show faith remains intact even when a person does not emigrate or when they give a greeting. This lesson examines those proofs and the conclusion that faith and its name are not removed by such omissions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the verses and conclusion sink in.
Notice how Maturidi uses direct Quranic evidence.
2
Identify the two Quranic proofs
Find the first verse: it affirms faith for those who believed but did not emigrate, yet denies full guardianship. Find the second verse: it forbids calling a believer a disbeliever based on a greeting.
Each verse distinguishes between faith and a specific action.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi states that 'what he says' – likely the view that such actions remove faith – does not remove faith nor its name. This refutes the idea that failing to emigrate or greet negates faith.
The phrase 'wa la ismahu' (nor its name) means the title of believer remains.
4
Reflect on the implication
Faith is robust; even important obligations like hijrah do not nullify it. This safeguards the understanding that faith is a state of conviction that survives imperfections in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال الله تعالى: 'وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَلَمْ يُهَاجِرُوا مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ وِلَايَتِهِمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ'، وقال: 'وَلَا تَقُولُوا لِمَنْ أَلْقَى إِلَيْكُمُ السَّلَامَ لَسْتَ مُؤْمِنًا'، ثبت أن الذي يقوله لا يزيل الإيمان ولا اسمه، والله أعلم.
And Allah Almighty said: 'And those who believed and did not emigrate – for you there is no guardianship of them at all', and He said: 'And do not say to one who gives you [the greeting of] peace, 'You are not a believer''. It is established that what he says does not remove faith nor its name. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 947

Commentary
This passage is a proof (دليل) that certain omitted actions do not negate faith. Maturidi cites two verses. First: 'And those who believed and did not emigrate – for you there is no guardianship of them at all' (Quran 8:72). This shows that even though faith is affirmed for them, they lack the full status of guardianship due to not emigrating. Second: 'And do not say to one who gives you peace, 'You are not a believer'' (Quran 4:94). This forbids calling a Muslim a disbeliever based on a statement. The conclusion: the statement that one makes (perhaps referring to an opponent's claim that certain actions remove faith) does not remove faith nor its name. The phrase 'ثبت أن الذي يقوله لا يزيل الإيمان ولا اسمه' means it is established that what the person says (i.e., the action or statement in question) does not negate iman or the title of believer.

Key Terms
إيمان
هجرة
ولاية
اسم الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that failing to perform hijrah (emigration) makes a person a non-believer.
Correction: The verse shows that those who believed but did not emigrate are still believers, though they lack full guardianship. Faith is not negated.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'وَلَا تَقُولُوا لِمَنْ أَلْقَى إِلَيْكُمُ السَّلَامَ لَسْتَ مُؤْمِنًا' teach?
A) Not to greet disbelievers
B) Not to call a Muslim a disbeliever based on a statement
C) To always investigate before judging
D) That emigrants are the only true believers

Key Takeaway
Faith remains intact even if one does not emigrate or fails to respond to a greeting; the Quran affirms their belief while noting separate consequences.

The Acceptance of Repentance is by Divine Grace, Not Perfect Action
Maturidi explains that the acceptance of repentance is by divine acceptance not physical action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Maturidi interprets the verse on repentance and prayer as referring to divine acceptance, not a condition for faith, and that the absence of an action does not negate faith.

Core Idea
Repentance is accepted by Allah's grace, not by flawless performance of prayer.

Maturidi addresses an opponent who used the verse 'But if they repent and establish prayer' to argue that faith depends on performing actions. He clarifies that the verse is about acceptance—when Allah accepts repentance, He does not wait for perfect performance. Let's explore this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice the structure: the opponent's proof, then Maturidi's rebuttal, then an additional example.
The phrase 'وفي الاعياء إلى حول' is unclear; treat it as a textual corruption.
2
Identify the opponent's argument
The opponent cites Quran 9:11 to argue that performing prayer is necessary for faith. Maturidi responds by shifting the focus from action to acceptance.
Maturidi uses the term 'قبول' (acceptance) to reinterpret the verse.
3
Understand the role of acceptance vs. action
Maturidi explains that if Allah required perfect action for acceptance, then brotherhood (in faith) would never be obligatory, and the door of repentance would be closed. This shows that acceptance is by grace.
4
Consider the example of emigration
Maturidi references the obligation of emigration (هجرة) which carried severe threats for neglect, yet Allah still affirmed the name of faith for those who did not emigrate. This reinforces that omission of an action does not negate faith.
This example is from a previous lesson, but it is used here as supporting evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد احتج بقوله: 'فَإِنْ تَابُوا وَأَقَامُوا الصَّلاةَ'، لكنا بينا أن ذلك في حق القبول؛ إذ لو ينتظر الفعل به لكان لا يجب الأخوة أبدا ولا يخلى سبيلهم وفي الاعياء إلى حول، وذلك مما لا معنى له. وقد بينا أمر الهجرة، وأنها كانت من الفرائض التي جاء في التخلف عنها الوعيد الشديد، ثم قد أثبت اسم الإيمان مع عدم ذلك، والله أعلم.
And he argued with His saying: 'But if they repent and establish prayer', but we explained that this concerns acceptance; for if He had waited for the action by it, brotherhood would never be obligatory, nor would the way be left for them, and in exhaustion to a year, and that has no meaning. And we have explained the matter of emigration, and that it was among the obligations concerning which severe threat came for abandoning it, yet He affirmed the name of faith despite its absence. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 948

Commentary
This passage is a response to an opponent's argument (احتج) using the verse 'But if they repent and establish prayer' (Quran 9:11). The opponent likely used this to argue that faith depends on performing actions like prayer. Maturidi explains that the verse refers to acceptance (قبول) – i.e., if they turn in repentance, Allah accepts them. If Allah had waited for the actual performance of the action (i.e., continuous prayer without fail), brotherhood would never be obligatory, and the way of repentance would be closed. The phrase 'وفي الاعياء إلى حول' is obscure but might mean 'and in exhaustion to a year' or perhaps something about being unable to perform. Maturidi then refers back to the earlier example of emigration (الهجرة), which was a heavy obligation with severe threats for neglecting it, yet Allah still affirmed the name of faith for those who did not emigrate (as in the previous lesson). So, the omission of an action does not remove faith.

أخوة
إقامة الصلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Repentance is only accepted if one performs prayer perfectly thereafter.
Correction: Maturidi explains that the verse refers to acceptance by God's grace; if perfect performance were required, repentance would never be obligatory because humans are fallible. The example of emigration shows that even grave omissions do not negate faith.

Checkpoint

B) The acceptance of repentance
C) The punishment for neglecting prayer
D) The obligation of emigration

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of repentance is based on divine grace, not on flawless fulfillment of actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?

Three Interpretations of 'La Yukhzi'
Maturidi presents three interpretations of the verse about God not disgracing the Prophet and believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three interpretations of the verse 'Yawma la yukhzi Allahu al-nabiyya' and how Maturidi uses them to refute the claim that believers face no punishment for major sins.

Core Idea
The verse promises believers escape from eternal disgrace, not immunity from all punishment.

Imam Maturidi here responds to an argument that the verse about God not disgracing the Prophet and believers proves that believers who commit major sins will not be punished at all. He unpacks the word 'yukhzi' (disgrace) to show it does not mean absence of punishment, but rather being spared from the ultimate disgrace of the disbelievers. Let's explore his three interpretations and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi presents three possible meanings of 'yukhzi'.
2
Identify the three interpretations
The passage explicitly lists three aspects (وجوه) of the verse. Find each one and note how each expands the meaning of 'disgrace'.
3
Understand the proof structure
See how Maturidi uses these interpretations to counter the claim that a believer cannot be punished. He shows that the verse is about a specific kind of disgrace, not all punishment.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this matters: it upholds divine justice (believers may be punished for sins) while maintaining divine mercy (they are spared eternal disgrace).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج بالآية التى فيها يَوْمَ لَا يَخْزِي اللَّهُ النَّبِيِّ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مَعَهُ، في صاحب الكبيرة إنه لو كان مؤمنا لكان لا يعذب ولا يوعد عليه. والآية إلى وجوه: أحدها أن لا يجزيه عن شفاعة رسول الله، بل يشفعه فيه وينجيه بها، والثانى أن يكون ذلك عندما يقول لهم: تواهنوا مظالمكم وعلى معذرتكم، والثالث أن يكون لا يجزيهم خزى الكفرة من الخلود في النار؛ إذ هو أنواع كما قال الله تعالى: لَيْسَ لَهُمْ طَعَامٌ إِلَّا مِنْ ضَرَيْع، وقال في موضع: فَلَيْسَ لَهُ الْيَوْمَ مَا هُنَا حَمِيمٌ، وَلَا طَعَامُ إِلَّا مِنْ غِسْلِيْن على اختلاف الأوقات، ويحتمل لا يجزى أى لا يفضح فيهنك ستره، كذلك في كل مؤمن. على اختلاف الدركات، فمثله وذلك.
Then he argued with the verse in which [it says] 'The Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him,' concerning the committer of a major sin: if he were a believer he would not be punished nor threatened. The verse has aspects: one is that He will not disgrace him through the intercession of the Messenger of Allah, but He will intercede for him and save him by it. The second is that this will be when He says to them: 'Forgive each other your wrongs and excuse yourselves.' The third is that He will not disgrace them by the disgrace of the disbelievers of eternity in the Fire; for it is of types as Allah said: 'They have no food except from dari' (thorny plant), and He said in another place: 'So he has no friend here today, and no food except from ghislin (pus)' according to differing times. And it is possible that 'He will not disgrace' means He will not expose, so He will cover them. Likewise for every believer, according to differing degrees. So its example is that.
Source pages p. 953

Commentary
This passage presents a proof and three interpretations of the verse 'Yawma la yukhzi Allahu al-nabiyya wa alladhina amanu ma'ahu' (Surah al-Tahrim: 8). The opponents argued that if the committer of a major sin were a believer, he would not be punished or threatened. Maturidi counters by offering three interpretations of 'yukhzi' (disgrace). First, God will not disgrace them by depriving them of the intercession of the Prophet; rather, He will accept the Prophet's intercession and save them. Second, the verse refers to the time when God will tell them to forgive each other's wrongs and make excuses. Third, 'disgrace' here means the disgrace of the disbelievers who will be eternally in the Fire, not that believers will not be punished at all. He supports this with Quranic verses showing different types of punishment (dari' and ghislin). He also suggests it could mean 'not expose' meaning conceal. So the verse does not prove that sinners escape punishment, but that they will not face the ultimate disgrace of the disbelievers.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Yawma la yukhzi…' guarantees that believers who commit major sins will never be punished at all.
Correction: Maturidi explains that 'la yukhzi' does not mean absence of all punishment; it means they will not be disgraced like the disbelievers (eternal shame) or will be saved through intercession/forgiveness.

Checkpoint

B) They will not be disgraced by being deprived of the Prophet's intercession
C) They will not commit sins
D) They will be granted wealth in Paradise

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's interpretations show that divine justice allows temporary punishment for believers while preserving them from eternal disgrace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you rely on the hope of the Prophet's intercession to feel comfortable, or does the possibility of temporary punishment in the grave or on the Day of Judgment drive you to repentance right now?
?
If, as the fourth interpretation suggests, God could expose every secret sin of yours on that Day, what is one hidden sin you need to confess and abandon starting today?
?
The lesson shows that punishment is graduated—even believers may face some form of punishment. Given that you know this, what will you change in your daily actions to reduce the accumulation of sins that might require purification?

The Specificity of Eternal Threat: Maturidi on Sin Names and Shirk
Maturidi classifies sin names and argues eternal threat is only for shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's classification of sin names from revelation and his argument that the eternal threat of punishment applies exclusively to shirk, not to other sins.

Core Idea
The eternal threat is specific to shirk alone.

This passage from Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid concludes his discussion of divine threats (wa'id). He analyzes the names of sins mentioned in revelation — fisq, fujur, isyan, zulm — showing that they are not all applied literally. He then establishes that only shirk carries the threat of eternal punishment, based on the nature of belief and human aversion to leaving religion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the technical terms for sin names and the concept of 'threat' (wa'id).
The Arabic may contain OCR errors; focus on the overall argument.
2
Identify the three types of sin names
Maturidi divides the names from revelation into three categories. Try to locate these three types in the text.
The passage states: 'among them is what may be permissible... among them is what is not permissible; and it is far-fetched...'
3
Understand the argument for specificity
Maturidi argues that because the names are divided and do not cover all sins, specificity (khsus) is established. The threat applies only where there is no doubt.
He warns that generalizing would lead to contradiction with other reports.
4
Analyze the evidence from human nature (fitra)
Maturidi provides evidence that eternal threat is only for shirk: humans are innately averse to leaving their religion, and beliefs are considered eternal by their adherents.
This shows that only shirk, which uproots religion, deserves eternal punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ رحمه الله : ثم جملة ما جاءت به الآثار في الوعيد بالتسمية من فسق و فجور أو عصيان أو ظلم أنها أسماء الخصال ثلاث : منها ما قاد يجوز في الحكمة على الإشارة إلى الفعل الذى سمى لأجله به غیر فسق ولا الأسماء الذميمة ، ومنها ما لا يجوز ، ومن البعيد قصد شيئين بينها هذا التباعد ، فحق ذلك أن يصرف إلى ما لا يرتاب فى الاسم والحكم، وإذا كان على أقسام ثلاثة ولم يتضمن كل الأقسام ثبت الخصوص في ذلك ، فازم مصرف ذلك إلى ما لا يشك فيه ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . على أن يصير غيره من في الصرف إلى العموم يحقق له التناقض المجيء أخبار العذم بذلك الخصوص ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثابت أو إذا احتمل الخصوص والعموم بما ينقسم المسمى به ما ذكرت فدق هما مثله الخوف لا القطع ، فمن قطع جرح يوجبه الحكمة غناء الشيء ، ولا قوة إلا بالله ثم الدلالة على وعيد الخلود لا يحتمله ما دون الشرك الأمر الذي جبل عليه الخلق من نفارهم عما به الخروج من أديانهم التي اعتقدوها وإن كانوا انتقادوها عقلا أو حجة أو تقليدا على وجود ما دون ذلك من الزلات فيهم وإن اختلفت ، فدل أن ذا مما جبل عليه الخلق ، بل أيد ذلك العقول ، إذ الاعتقادات تكون عند أربابها أبديات ، ولا كذلك الأفعال التي تشار إليها وعلى ذلك أضدادها ، وكذلك السمع فى الأفعال المشارة أنها على الاختلاف ، فعلى ذلك أديانهم
The Shaykh (rahimahullah) said: Then the summary of what the transmitted reports (athar) have come with regarding the threat (wa'id) by naming (tasmia) of fisq, fujur, isyan, or zulm — that they are names of three types of traits: among them is what may be permissible in wisdom to point to the action for which it was named, other than fisq and blameworthy names; and among them is what is not permissible; and it is far-fetched to aim at two things between which is such divergence. So the right thing is to direct it to that which there is no doubt in the name and the ruling. And if it is upon three divisions and does not include all divisions, then specificity (khsus) is established in that. So direct that application to what there is no doubt in. And there is no power except with Allah. Such that (if) one makes other than that in directing to generality (umum), it would realize for him the contradiction of the coming reports of punishment with that specificity. And there is no power except with Allah. Confirmed. Or if it admits of specificity and generality according to what the named thing is divided into — what I mentioned — then the fear (n) of it is like the fear (n), not the cutting (n). So whoever cuts a wound that wisdom necessitates as sufficiency of the thing. And there is no power except with Allah. Then the evidence that the threat of eternity (khulud) cannot be borne by what is less than shirk — the matter on which the creation has been innately disposed (jibillah) from their aversion to what causes exit from their religions which they have believed in, even if they have criticized them (intaqaduha) by reason, proof, or imitation (taqlid); (they are averse) to the existence of that which is less than that from slips (zallat) among them, even if they differ. So this indicates that this is part of the innate disposition (jibillah) of creation. Rather, intellects support that, because beliefs are, for their adherents, eternal (abadiyyat), and not so are the actions that are pointed to; and upon that are their opposites. And likewise revelation (sam') regarding the actions pointed to is that they are upon difference. So upon that are their religions.
Source pages p. 962

Commentary
This passage is a concluding summary by the Shaykh (likely Maturidi himself) on the issue of divine threats (wa'id) as mentioned in transmitted reports (athar). He states that the names used in threats — fisq (immorality), fujur (wickedness), isyan (disobedience), and zulm (injustice) — actually refer to three types of traits (khisas). The first type is what may be permissible in wisdom to apply to an action other than the specific name, meaning the name might be used metaphorically or in a non-literal sense. The second type is what is not permissible to be applied to actions other than the named. The third type involves a far-fetched combination of two attributes. Given this classification, the correct course is to apply the threat only to what is undoubted in its name and ruling (i.e., shirk). Since the names are divided into three categories, and not all categories are included (i.e., the threat does not apply to all), this proves specificity (khsus). Therefore, one must restrict the application of the threat to what is certain. Any attempt to generalize (ta'mim) would lead to contradiction with the specific reports. Then Maturidi provides evidence that the threat of eternal punishment (khulud) can only be for shirk, because human nature (jibillah) is innately averse to anything that would cause them to exit their religion, even if they have adopted that religion through reason, proof, or blind imitation. The presence of lesser sins among them does not change this. Furthermore, intellects (uql) support this because beliefs are considered eternal by their adherents, unlike actions which are variable. Similarly, revelation (sam') indicates that actions are subject to differing rulings. Therefore, the eternal threat is specific to shirk, the only action that completely uproots the religion.

Misconception: All sins mentioned in revelation (like fisq, fujur, etc.) carry the same threat of eternal punishment.
Correction: Maturidi argues that these sin names are of three types, and the threat applies only where it is certain, which is only shirk. Lesser sins do not entail eternal punishment.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that the threat of eternal punishment is specific to shirk, based on the classification of sin names and the innate human aversion to leaving one's religion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, have you ever assumed that certain sins might lead to eternal punishment while downplaying the gravity of shirk in your heart? Examine your beliefs: do you truly feel the terror of associating partners with Allah as the only unforgivable sin, or do you treat other sins with equal dread? Let this lesson push you to recalibrate your fear of Allah according to His revelation.
?
Consider the innate aversion you feel when someone challenges your core beliefs. Maturidi points out that humans innately recoil from leaving their religion, even if it was adopted by imitation. When was the last time you felt that aversion, not for a minor opinion but for the very foundation of iman? How does that instinct reflect the reality that only shirk is fit for eternal punishment? Let this question stay with you until you purify your tawhid.
?
If your beliefs are eternal for you, as Maturidi says, do your actions reflect that eternity? You may have slipped into minor sins without a second thought, but have you ever feared that your lack of attention to shirk in your daily thoughts and words could be the very thing that separates you from Allah's mercy? This lesson calls you to take stock: are you more concerned with avoiding small sins while neglecting the greatest sin of all? Repent and strengthen your tawhid.

Intercession Does Not Justify Sin
Maturidi refutes the objection against intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hope of intercession does not justify committing major sins, and how Imam Maturidi refutes that objection.

Core Idea
Intercession is earned by good deeds, not by sinning.

Some argued that if intercession is available for major sinners, then people might sin deliberately to qualify for it. Imam Maturidi rejects this as a misunderstanding. He explains that intercession is earned through obedience and repentance, not through sin itself. This lesson walks through his clear reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Maturidi's response
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi begins by stating the objection and then immediately labels it a 'delusion'.
The objection claims that swearing to sin to earn intercession would command sin.
2
Understand the key distinction
Maturidi distinguishes between the one for whom intercession is made and the one who earns intercession. Identify this distinction in the text.
Intercession is earned through good deeds, not by committing sins.
3
Follow the analogy with minor sins
Maturidi draws a parallel: just as one is not told to commit minor sins to seek forgiveness, one is not told to commit major sins to gain intercession.
The logic is consistent: avoid sins, repent, and obey.
4
Note the scriptural foundation
Maturidi affirms that intercession is established by the Qur'an and Sunnah. Recognize how he uses this to ground the discussion.
Intercession is a proven doctrine, not a human invention.
5
Reflect on the nature of intercession
Maturidi describes intercession as occurring for slips that deserve wrath, forgiven through the righteous. Consider how this aligns with mercy, not license.
Intercession is for those who slip, not those who persist in sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة الشفاعة. ثم قال بعضهم: لو كانت الكبيرة مما يجوز الشفاعة له لكان من يحلف بفعل شيء يستوجب به الشفاعة يؤمر بارتكاب الكبيرة. قال الفقيه رحمه الله: فنقول ذلك وهم؛ لأنه ليس الذي له يشفع هو الذي به يستوجب الشفاعة، بل يستوجب بالحسنات التي بها يجب الولاية فما ترك فحق من حلف بذلك ليس أن يقال له: اعص، ولكن يقال له: اطع، ليستوجب به الشفاعة فما عصيت، وكذلك من يخلف: لا فعلن الفعل الذي استوجب به المغفرة، لا يقال له ارتكب الصغائر، بل يؤمر باتقاء الكبائر والتوبة عنها ليغفر له، فمثله أمر الشفاعة. والشفاعة من أعظم ما احتج بها، وقد جاء القرآن بها والآثار عن رسول الله. والشفاعة في المعهود والمتعالم من الأمر تكون عند زلات يستوجب بها المقت والعقوبة، فيعفى عن مرتكبها بشفاعة الأخيار وأهل الرضا، ثم كانت الصغائر
The Issue of Intercession. Then some of them said: If the major sin were such that intercession is permissible for its doer, then one who swears to do something by which he obtains intercession would be commanded to commit the major sin. The jurist (may God have mercy on him) said: We say that is a delusion; because the one for whom intercession is made is not the one by whom intercession is earned. Rather, he earns it through good deeds by which friendship is obligated. So what is left? The right of one who swears by that is not that he be told: 'Sin', but rather he is told: 'Obey', so that he may earn intercession by it, and not that he sins. Likewise, one who says: 'I will not do the act by which I earn forgiveness' is not told to commit minor sins, but is commanded to avoid major sins and repent from them so that he may be forgiven. Such is the matter of intercession. And intercession is among the greatest proofs employed. The Qur'an and the reports from the Messenger of God have come with it. And intercession, according to what is customary and well-known in the matter, occurs at times of slips that earn wrath and punishment, so the perpetrator is forgiven through the intercession of the righteous and those who are pleased. Then the minor sins...
Source pages p. 964

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection against the doctrine of intercession (shafa'a) for major sinners. The objection claims that if intercession is permissible for major sins, then a person who swears to do something that earns intercession would be commanded to commit a major sin to obtain it. Imam Maturidi, citing 'the jurist' (likely himself or a teacher), refutes this as a delusion. He explains that the one who is interceded for is not the one who earns intercession. Rather, intercession is earned through good deeds, which obligate friendship (wilaya). So one who swears to do something should be told to obey, not to sin, in order to earn intercession. Similarly, one who vows not to do the act that earns forgiveness is not told to commit minor sins, but to avoid major sins and repent. Thus the objection is based on a misunderstanding. Maturidi then affirms that intercession is a proven doctrine from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and describes its customary nature: it occurs at times of slips (zallat) that deserve wrath and punishment, and the perpetrator is forgiven through the intercession of the righteous. The passage ends with a reference to minor sins, possibly continuing the argument that intercession applies also to minor sins but the text is cut off.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: Intercession is earned through good deeds and repentance, not by sinning. One is commanded to obey, not sin, to obtain it.

Instead of passively hoping for intercession, what concrete act of repentance or good deed can you perform today to actively earn that mercy? Be honest: what is holding you back from doing it?

Refuting the Claim That Intercession Encourages Sin
Maturidi refutes an objection about intercession and explains its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why intercession does not encourage sin and how it is earned through good deeds.

Core Idea
Intercession is earned by obedience, not disobedience.

Some argue that belief in intercession for major sins encourages people to sin, thinking they will be forgiven anyway. Imam Maturidi refutes this misconception by clarifying that intercession is not earned by sin but by good deeds. In this passage, he explains the correct understanding of intercession and warns against rejecting it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The opponent claims that if major sins can be forgiven through intercession, then a person swearing to do something that earns intercession would be commanded to sin. Read the Arabic and translation carefully.
The objection is a hypothetical syllogism.
2
Understand the refutation
Maturidi calls the objection an illusion. He distinguishes between the one who intercedes and the one for whom intercession is made; intercession is earned through good deeds, not sin.
Focus on the phrase 'ليس الذي له يشفع هو الذي به يستوجب الشفاعة'.
3
See the analogy
Maturidi provides an analogy: just as a person who vows not to do an act earning forgiveness is told to avoid major sins and repent, not to commit minor sins, so too with intercession.
The analogy reinforces that obedience, not disobedience, is commanded.
4
Grasp the nature of intercession
Intercession applies to slips deserving punishment; minor sins are not punishable for those believing in eternal punishment for major sins, and disbelievers are not pardoned.
This limits the scope of intercession.
5
Consider the consequences of rejection
Rejecting intercession invalidates the Qur'an and traditions, destroys hope in Allah's mercy, and nullifies Muslim supplication for intercession.
Maturidi warns of grave implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة الشفاعة ثم قال بعضهم: لو كانت الكبيرة مما يجوز الشفاعة له لكان من يحلف بفعل شيء يستوجب به الشفاعة يؤمر بارتكاب الكبيرة قال الفقيه رحمه الله: فنقول ذلك وهم؛ لأنه ليس الذي له يشفع هو الذي به يستوجب الشفاعة، بل يستوجب بالحسنات التي بها يجب الولاية فما ترك فحق من حلف بذلك ليس أن يقال له: اعص، ولكن يقال له: اطع ليستوجب به الشفاعة فما عصيت، وكذلك من يخلف: لا فعلن الفعل الذي استوجب به المغفرة، لا يقال له ارتكب الصغائر، بل يؤمر باتقاء الكبائر والتوبة عنها ليغفر له، فمثله أمر الشفاعة. والشفاعة من أعظم ما احتج بها، وقد جاء القرآن بها والآثار عن رسول الله. والشفاعة في المعهود والمتعالم من الأمر تكون عند زلات يستوجب بها المقت والعقوبة، فيعفى عن مرتكبها بشفاعة الأخيار وأهل الرضا، ثم كانت الصغائر عنهم مما لا يجوز التعذيب عليها عند القائلين بالخلود في الكبائر، والكفار مما لا يعفى بالشفاعة، فإذا بطل عظيم ما جاء به من القرآن والآثار في الامتنان، وسقط ما جبل عليه أهل العلم من الرجا بالله وبرحمته، ويبطل دعاء المسلمين بشفاعة الرسل، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The issue of intercession. Then some of them said: If the major sin were such that intercession is permissible for it, then one who swears to do something by which he earns intercession would be commanded to commit a major sin. The faqih (Imam Maturidi) said, may Allah have mercy on him: We say: This is an illusion; because the one for whom intercession is made is not the one through whom intercession is earned. Rather, it is earned through good deeds by which [divine] friendship is required. So whoever leaves [good deeds] — the one who swears to that should not be told: 'Sin', but rather he should be told: 'Obey' in order to earn intercession thereby, so do not disobey. Similarly, one who says: 'I will not do the act by which I earned forgiveness' — he is not told to commit minor sins, but rather he is commanded to avoid major sins and repent from them so that he may be forgiven. Such is the matter of intercession. And intercession is among the greatest proofs that have been adduced; the Qur'an has come with it and the traditions from the Messenger of Allah. And intercession in the customary and well-known matter occurs at times of slips that deserve wrath and punishment, whereby the perpetrator is forgiven through the intercession of the righteous and the people of approval. Then minor sins from them are such that punishment is not permissible for them according to those who hold eternal punishment for major sins, and the disbelievers are such that they are not pardoned through intercession. So if the great [benefit] of what has come from the Qur'an and traditions in the bestowal of grace becomes invalid, and what the people of knowledge have been disposed to in hoping in Allah and His mercy falls away, and the Muslims' supplication for the intercession of the messengers becomes void — and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 964

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against intercession for major sins: if major sins can be forgiven through intercession, then someone who swears to do something that earns intercession would be commanded to sin. The author refutes this by distinguishing between the one who intercedes and the one for whom intercession is made; intercession is earned through good deeds, not sin. He also explains the nature of intercession: it occurs for slips that deserve punishment, and minor sins are not punished for those who believe in eternal punishment for major sins. The author warns that rejecting intercession would invalidate the Qur'an and traditions and undermine the hope of Muslims.

Key Terms

الولاية
الزلات

العقوبة
الأخيار
أهل الرضا
الصغائر
الكبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession encourages people to commit major sins because they think they will be forgiven anyway.
Correction: Intercession is earned through good deeds, not sin; therefore it does not encourage sin but obedience.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what earns intercession?
A) Swearing to commit a major sin.
B) Good deeds that necessitate divine friendship.
C) Avoiding all sins.
D) Supplication only.

Key Takeaway
Intercession is earned through obedience, not sin, and rejecting it undermines the Qur'an and hope in Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you find yourself relying on the hope of intercession to keep sinning, or does that hope push you to repent and obey more? What will you do today to ensure your hope leads to action?
?
The passage says intercession is earned by good deeds, not by sins. Look at your daily routine: are your actions actually earning that intercession, or are you assuming it will come without effort? What one change can you make this week to start earning it?
?
If intercession were truly a free pass, what would that say about Allah's justice? How does understanding that intercession requires obedience affect the way you view your relationship with Allah?
